### ?? THE CONTEXT (COMPOUND INTELLIGENCE)
In our previous session, our adversarial review shattered our naive assumptions. We discovered that our planned fixes (a simple Generation counter and Callback-only OrderId mapping) introduce 5 catastrophic new traps in our lock-free architecture:

1. **The 64-bit Packing Race**: Generation and State must be updated atomically, requiring 64-bit packing, but 32-bit generations overflow in 4.9 days under high load.
2. **Callback-Only Deadlock (Event Loss Window)**: Waiting for `OnAccountOrderUpdate` to map the OrderId creates a 50-500ms window where async partial-fills drop into the void.
3. **Compound Callback Race**: If a slot is freed and reallocated before a delayed callback arrives, the callback fails the generation check and the order becomes unmanaged.
4. **`ConcurrentDictionary` Allocation Violation**: Fixing the thread-safety of `_orderIdToFsmKey` using `ConcurrentDictionary` violates our strict Zero-Allocation hot-path mandate.
5. **Missing Circuit Breaker**: We have no global primitive to halt submissions during broker network disconnects, guaranteeing infinite retry loops and queue exhaustion.

### ??? THE MISSION: DESIGN THE SOLUTIONS
You are acting as the V12 Lead Architect. You must design the implementation patterns that solve these 5 traps while strictly adhering to our core DNA. 

Please provide an **Architectural Repair Report** that defines the following:

1. **The FSM State Struct**: Write the exact C# `struct` layout and bit-shifting logic required to pack the FSM State, Generation Counter, and a potential "Pending" flag into a single 64-bit `long` for use with `Interlocked.CompareExchange`. Explain how we handle the 32-bit wrap-around safely.
2. **Pre-Submit Registration**: Design the lifecycle flow to solve the OrderId deadlock. How do we register a "Pending" order ID *before* it hits the async broker network, without exposing it to premature execution?
3. **Zero-Allocation Hash Map**: Since `ConcurrentDictionary` allocates heavily, propose a zero-allocation, lock-free routing alternative for `_orderIdToFsmKey` (e.g., a pre-allocated lock-free array map or ring-based routing table).
4. **The Circuit Breaker**: Define the C# state machine for a lock-free Global Submit Circuit Breaker (Closed -> Half-Open -> Open) using `Interlocked` counters for failure thresholds.

### ??? THE V12 DNA CONSTRAINTS
- **Zero-Lock Policy**: `lock(stateLock)` is STRICTLY BANNED. Use atomic primitives.
- **Zero-Allocation**: Hot-paths must not allocate on the heap.

You MUST output your entire response wrapped inside a single ```markdown ... ``` code block. This ensures the chat interface renders a native "Copy" button in the top right corner of the block, allowing the Director to cleanly copy your entire report in one click.

# V12 Compound Architectural Repair Report

## 1. FSM State Struct (64-bit Packing)
**Layout (from MSB to LSB):**
- 8 bits: State (0-255)
- 1 bit: Pending flag
- 55 bits: Generation counter (wrap-safe, monotonic)

**C# Struct + Bit Packing**
struct FsmPackedState
{
    private const int StateShift = 56;
    private const int PendingShift = 55;
    private const long PendingMask = 1L << PendingShift;
    private const long GenerationMask = (1L << 55) - 1;

    public static long Pack(byte state, bool pending, long generation)
    {
        var gen = generation & GenerationMask;
        var pend = pending ? PendingMask : 0;
        return ((long)state << StateShift) | pend | gen;
    }

    public static void Unpack(long value, out byte state, out bool pending, out long generation)
    {
        state = (byte)(value >> StateShift);
        pending = (value & PendingMask) != 0;
        generation = value & GenerationMask;
    }
}

**Wrap-Safety:**
Generation uses 55 bits (~1.1e16). At 1M ops/sec, wrap occurs after ~347 years.
When comparing generations, only reject callbacks with mismatched generation; wrap is
so distant that simple equality remains safe.

## 2. Pre-Submit Registration (Pending Lifecycle)
1. Reserve slot -> compute fsmKey + generation.
2. Publish packed state as (State=Submitting, Pending=true, Generation=gen) via Interlocked.
3. Register OrderId -> fsmKey in routing table before sending to broker.
4. Dispatch order async.
5. On ack/callback, flip Pending=false and advance to Active state.
6. Any fill arriving before ack routes via OrderId map to the Pending slot.

**Guarantee:** no fill is dropped, and Pending orders never execute without a registered slot.

## 3. Zero-Allocation Hash Map (OrderId -> FSM Key)
**Pattern:** pre-allocated, lock-free open-addressing table.
- Fixed-size array of structs: {long orderId, int fsmKey, long generation}
- Index = (orderId * 11400714819323198485ul) >> shift
- Linear probing; updates use Interlocked.CompareExchange on orderId field
- Freeing a slot zeroes orderId (0 = empty)
- Table sized for max concurrent orders to avoid resize allocations

**Read Path:**
Spin probe; if orderId matches and generation matches, route to slot. No heap allocs.

## 4. Global Submit Circuit Breaker
**States:** 0=Closed, 1=HalfOpen, 2=Open

struct SubmitCircuit
{
    private long _state; // packed: state (2 bits) + failureCount (62 bits)
    private const int StateShift = 62;
    private const long FailureMask = (1L << 62) - 1;

    public bool AllowSubmit(int failThreshold, long nowTicks, long openUntilTicks)
    {
        var snapshot = Interlocked.Read(ref _state);
        var state = (int)(snapshot >> StateShift);
        var failures = snapshot & FailureMask;

        if (state == 2 && nowTicks < openUntilTicks) return false;
        if (state == 2 && nowTicks >= openUntilTicks) return TryHalfOpen(snapshot);
        if (state == 1 && failures > 0) return false; // single probe
        return true;
    }

    public void RecordFailure(int failThreshold, long nowTicks, long openUntilTicks)
    {
        long snapshot;
        do
        {
            snapshot = Interlocked.Read(ref _state);
            var state = (int)(snapshot >> StateShift);
            var failures = (snapshot & FailureMask) + 1;
            var nextState = state;
            if (failures >= failThreshold) nextState = 2; // Open
            var next = ((long)nextState << StateShift) | failures;
        }
        while (Interlocked.CompareExchange(ref _state, next, snapshot) != snapshot);
    }

    private bool TryHalfOpen(long snapshot)
    {
        var next = (1L << StateShift); // state = HalfOpen, failures = 0
        return Interlocked.CompareExchange(ref _state, next, snapshot) == snapshot;
    }
}

**Behavior:**
- Closed: all submits allowed until failure threshold.
- Open: rejects until cooldown tick.
- HalfOpen: allows exactly one probe; success resets to Closed.

TRAP #1CRITICAL
The 64-bit Packing Race
Generation and State must be updated atomically, requiring 64-bit packing, but 32-bit generations overflow in 4.9 days under high load.
??THE TRAP
* •The FSM slot state and a generation counter are stored in separate fields.
* •Updating them separately creates a TOCTOU race: Thread A reads state=Active, Thread B frees the slot and increments generation, Thread A writes state=Free — corrupting the new occupant's state.
* •Using Interlocked.CompareExchange on a single 64-bit value solves the atomicity, but packing requires careful bit allocation.
* •A naive 32-bit generation counter wraps in ~4.9 days at 10K ops/sec, causing ABA problems where old callbacks match new slots.
???THE SOLUTION: Packed 64-bit FSM State with Safe Generation Wrap-Around
* ?Pack State (16 bits), Generation (32 bits), and a Pending flag (1 bit) into a single 64-bit long.
* ?Use Interlocked.CompareExchange for all state transitions — this is the ONLY way to guarantee atomicity.
* ?Handle 32-bit wrap-around by treating generation as a monotonic counter that wraps to 1 (never 0) and using a "generation gap" check to detect ABA.
* ?The Pending flag (bit 63) allows pre-registration of OrderIds before broker submission completes.
* ?Remaining 15 bits are reserved for future expansion (circuit breaker slot flags, etc.).

??KEY INSIGHTS
* 1.All state transitions go through TryTransition() — no direct field writes allowed.
* 2.Generation increments on EVERY transition, not just slot reuse. This makes every state change uniquely identifiable.
* 3.The wrap-to-1 (never 0) strategy creates a definitive generation gap. A callback with gen=0x00000000 can never match a slot at gen=0x00000001.
* 4.Reserved bits (48-63) are future-proofing: circuit breaker flags, priority hints, or debug markers can be added without changing the struct layout.
* 5.The CAS loop includes a spin counter for diagnostics — if spins > 10, log a contention warning.
??
TRAP #2CRITICAL
Callback-Only Deadlock (Event Loss Window)
Waiting for OnAccountOrderUpdate to map the OrderId creates a 50-500ms window where async partial-fills drop into the void.
??THE TRAP
* •Current flow: Submit order ? wait for broker ack ? OnAccountOrderUpdate fires ? map OrderId to FsmKey ? begin managing fills.
* •The 50-500ms gap between submission and callback is the "Event Loss Window" — any partial fills arriving in this window have no FsmKey to route to.
* •Under high-frequency trading conditions, partial fills can arrive within milliseconds of submission.
* •Lost fills = lost money. This is not a theoretical concern.
???THE SOLUTION: Pre-Submit Registration with Pending State
* ?Register the OrderId-to-FsmKey mapping BEFORE the async broker call, using the Pending flag in the packed state.
* ?The flow becomes: Allocate slot ? Set state=Pending ? Register OrderId ? Submit to broker ? On callback, transition Pending?Submitted?Active.
* ?The Pending flag (bit 0) acts as a "do not execute" marker — callbacks that arrive during this window are queued, not dropped.
* ?A lock-free pending queue buffers early fills until the OrderId mapping is confirmed.
* ?If the broker submission fails, the slot is atomically transitioned back to Free and the OrderId mapping is removed.
Pre-Submit Registration Flow
Show OLD Flow (Broken)
The fixed flow: OrderId mapped BEFORE broker submission — eliminates the Event Loss Window entirely.
[PRE-SUBMIT]~10ns
Circuit Breaker Check
Verify the global circuit breaker allows submissions. If Open, reject immediately.
[PRE-SUBMIT]~50ns
Allocate Free Slot
Find and claim a free slot from the slot allocator using lock-free CAS.
[PRE-SUBMIT]~20ns
Set Pending State
Atomically set the slot to Pending state with the Pending flag (bit 0). This is the critical step.
[PRE-SUBMIT]~100ns
Register OrderId ? FsmKey
Map the OrderId to the FsmKey in the zero-allocation hash router. Now callbacks can be routed.
[BROKER I/O]50-500ms ??
Submit to Broker (Async)
Send the order to the broker asynchronously. This is the ONLY blocking operation — and it's off the hot path.
[BROKER I/O]~30ns
Early Fills Buffered
If partial fills arrive during the Pending window, they are queued in the lock-free PendingFillQueue — NOT dropped.
[ACK]~200ns
Broker Acknowledges
OnBrokerAck fires. Validate generation, transition Pending ? Submitted, drain pending fills.
[ACK]~20ns
Transition to Active
Final transition: Submitted ? Active. The order is now fully managed. All fills processed.
?KEY INSIGHT
The Pending flag (bit 0) is the critical innovation. By setting it BEFORE the async broker call, we create a "safe zone" where callbacks are recognized but deferred. The Event Loss Window is eliminated — fills are either processed immediately or buffered, never dropped.

FsmPackedState.TryTransition(                class="kw">ref slot.StateValue,                FsmPackedState.Create(FsmState.Submitted, fsmKey.Generation + 1),                FsmState.Active,                class="kw">out _);        }    }    class="kw">private class="kw">void RollbackSubmission(int slotIndex, uint generation)    {        class="kw">ref var slot = class="kw">ref _slots.GetSlot(slotIndex);        var expected = FsmPackedState.Create(            FsmState.Pending, generation, pending: class="kw">true);        class="kw">if (FsmPackedState.TryTransition(            class="kw">ref slot.StateValue, expected, FsmState.Free, class="kw">out _))        {            _slots.Free(slotIndex);        }    }}
PendingFillQueue.cs — Lock-Free Early Fill Buffer62 lines

class="cm">/// <summary>class="cm">/// Lock-free ring buffer class="kw">for fills that arrive before theclass="cm">/// OrderId mapping is confirmed (during the Pending window).class="cm">/// Pre-allocated — zero heap allocation class="kw">in the hot path.class="cm">/// </summary>class="kw">public sealed class PendingFillQueue{    class="kw">private class="kw">readonly FillEntry[] _buffer;    class="kw">private class="kw">readonly int _mask;    class="kw">private long _head; class="cm">// CAS-updated    class="kw">private long _tail; class="cm">// CAS-updated    class="kw">public PendingFillQueue(int capacity = 1024)    {        class="cm">// Capacity must be power of 2 class="kw">for mask-based indexing        _buffer = class="kw">new FillEntry[capacity];        _mask = capacity - 1;        _head = 0;        _tail = 0;    }    class="cm">/// <summary>    class="cm">/// Enqueue a fill event. Returns class="kw">false class="kw">if queue is full.    class="cm">/// </summary>    class="kw">public bool Enqueue(FillEvent fill)    {        long tail, head, next;        class="kw">do        {            tail = Volatile.Read(class="kw">ref _tail);            head = Volatile.Read(class="kw">ref _head);            next = tail + 1;            class="kw">if (next - head > _mask) class="kw">return class="kw">false; class="cm">// Full        }        class="kw">while (Interlocked.CompareExchange(class="kw">ref _tail, next, tail) != tail);        _buffer[tail & _mask] = fill;        class="kw">return class="kw">true;    }    class="cm">/// <summary>    class="cm">/// Drain all fills class="kw">for a specific OrderId and process them.    class="cm">/// Called when the OrderId mapping is confirmed.    class="cm">/// </summary>    class="kw">public class="kw">void Drain(string orderId, Action<FillEvent> processor)    {        long head = Volatile.Read(class="kw">ref _head);        long tail = Volatile.Read(class="kw">ref _tail);        class="kw">for (long i = head; i < tail; i++)        {            class="kw">ref var entry = class="kw">ref _buffer[i & _mask];            class="kw">if (entry.OrderId == orderId)            {                processor(entry.Fill);                entry = class="kw">default; class="cm">// Clear after processing                Volatile.Write(class="kw">ref _head, i + 1);            }        }    }}
??KEY INSIGHTS
* 1.The Pending flag is the key innovation — it marks slots as "registered but not yet confirmed," allowing the router to accept callbacks while deferring execution.
* 2.The PendingFillQueue is a bounded SPSC ring buffer — single producer (callback thread), single consumer (ack handler). No locks needed.
* 3.Rollback on failure is atomic: the CAS ensures we only free the slot if it's still in the Pending state with the expected generation.
* 4.This eliminates the 50-500ms Event Loss Window entirely — fills are either processed immediately or buffered, never dropped.
??
TRAP #3HIGH
Compound Callback Race
If a slot is freed and reallocated before a delayed callback arrives, the callback fails the generation check and the order becomes unmanaged.
??THE TRAP
* •Thread A frees slot 42 (generation 5). Thread B allocates slot 42 (generation 6). A delayed callback for generation 5 arrives.
* •The generation check correctly rejects the callback — but now the order from generation 5 is permanently unmanaged.
* •This is a correctness issue: the order's state is unknown, fills are lost, and risk management is compromised.
* •The root cause is that freeing a slot destroys the order's identity before all callbacks have been processed.
???THE SOLUTION: Graceful Callback Degradation with Tombstone Routing
* ?When a callback fails the generation check, instead of silently dropping it, route it to a "tombstone" handler.
* ?The tombstone handler logs the orphaned event and attempts recovery via the OrderId (which remains valid even if the slot is reused).
* ?Implement a "delayed free" mechanism: slots enter a Tombstone state for a configurable grace period (e.g., 30 seconds) before becoming truly Free.
* ?During the Tombstone state, the OrderId mapping is preserved but the slot cannot be reallocated.
* ?A background sweeper transitions Tombstone slots to Free after the grace period expires.

class="kw">public sealed class CallbackHandler{    class="kw">private class="kw">readonly SlotAllocator _slots;    class="kw">private class="kw">readonly OrderIdRouter _router;    class="kw">private class="kw">readonly TombstoneRegistry _tombstones;    class="cm">/// <summary>    class="cm">/// Handle an incoming fill/cancel/ack callback.    class="cm">/// Uses generation check + tombstone fallback class="kw">for safety.    class="cm">/// </summary>    class="kw">public class="kw">void HandleCallback(CallbackEvent evt)    {        var fsmKey = _router.Resolve(evt.OrderId);        class="kw">if (fsmKey == class="kw">default)        {            class="cm">// OrderId not found — check tombstones            HandleTombstoneCallback(evt);            class="kw">return;        }        class="kw">ref var slot = class="kw">ref _slots.GetSlot(fsmKey.SlotIndex);        long currentState = Volatile.Read(class="kw">ref slot.StateValue);        var state = class="kw">new FsmPackedState(currentState);        class="cm">// ?? Generation Check ??????????????????????????????        class="kw">if (fsmKey.Generation != state.Generation)        {            class="cm">// GENERATION MISMATCH: Slot was reused.            class="cm">// Route to tombstone handler class="kw">for recovery. TombstoneRegistry.cs — Delayed Free Mechanism76 lines
CollapseCopy
class="cm">/// <summary>class="cm">/// Manages tombstone entries class="kw">for slots that have been freedclass="cm">/// but may still receive delayed callbacks.class="cm">/// Pre-allocated array — zero allocation class="kw">in hot path.class="cm">/// </summary>class="kw">public sealed class TombstoneRegistry{    class="kw">private class="kw">readonly TombstoneEntry[] _entries;    class="kw">private class="kw">readonly long _gracePeriodTicks;    class="kw">private int _count;    class="kw">public TombstoneRegistry(int capacity, TimeSpan gracePeriod)    {        _entries = class="kw">new TombstoneEntry[capacity];        _gracePeriodTicks = gracePeriod.Ticks;        _count = 0;    }    class="cm">/// <summary>    class="cm">/// Register a tombstone when a slot is freed.    class="cm">/// The OrderId mapping is preserved class="kw">for the grace period.    class="cm">/// </summary>    class="kw">public class="kw">void Register(string orderId, FsmKey key, OrderSnapshot snapshot)    {        int index = Interlocked.Increment(class="kw">ref _count) - 1;        class="kw">if (index >= _entries.Length)        {            class="cm">// Registry full — log and skip            class="cm">// (This should never happen with proper capacity)            class="kw">return;        }        _entries[index] = class="kw">new TombstoneEntry        {            OrderId = orderId,            Key = key,            Snapshot = snapshot,            ExpiresAt = DateTime.UtcNow.Ticks + _gracePeriodTicks,            IsActive = class="kw">true        };    }    class="kw">public TombstoneEntry? Lookup(string orderId)    {        class="kw">for (int i = 0; i < _count; i++)        {            class="kw">ref var entry = class="kw">ref _entries[i];            class="kw">if (entry.IsActive && entry.OrderId == orderId)            {                class="kw">if (DateTime.UtcNow.Ticks > entry.ExpiresAt)                {                    entry.IsActive = class="kw">false; class="cm">// Expired                    class="kw">return class="kw">null;                }                class="kw">return entry;            }        }        class="kw">return class="kw">null;    }    class="cm">/// <summary>    class="cm">/// Sweep expired tombstones. Call periodically from    class="cm">/// a background thread (not class="kw">in the hot path).    class="cm">/// </summary>    class="kw">public class="kw">void Sweep()    {        long now = DateTime.UtcNow.Ticks;        class="kw">for (int i = 0; i < _count; i++)        {            class="kw">if (_entries[i].IsActive && now > _entries[i].ExpiresAt)            {                _entries[i].IsActive = class="kw">false;            }        }    }}
??KEY INSIGHTS
* 1.The tombstone pattern trades a small amount of memory (pre-allocated array) for correctness — no order is ever silently lost.
* 2.The grace period should be tuned to your broker's maximum callback latency. Start with 30s and measure.
* 3.The OrderIdRouter mapping is NOT removed when a slot is freed — it remains valid until the tombstone expires.
* 4.The Sweep() method runs on a background timer, not in the hot path. It's O(n) but n is bounded by the tombstone capacity.
???
TRAP #4HIGH
ConcurrentDictionary Allocation Violation
Fixing the thread-safety of _orderIdToFsmKey using ConcurrentDictionary violates our strict Zero-Allocation hot-path mandate.
??THE TRAP
* •ConcurrentDictionary<TKey, TValue> allocates Node objects, bucket arrays, and lock objects on every insertion.
* •Under high-frequency order flow (10K+ orders/sec), this generates megabytes of garbage per second.
* •GC pauses of even 1ms can cause missed market opportunities and slippage.
* •The hot path (order submission + callback routing) must be zero-allocation.
???THE SOLUTION: Lock-Free Open Addressing Hash Map with Pre-Allocated Storage
* ?Replace ConcurrentDictionary with a pre-allocated open-addressing hash table using linear probing.
* ?All storage is allocated once at startup — zero heap allocation during operation.
* ?Use Interlocked.CompareExchange for lock-free insertions and a two-phase deletion (tombstone marker + background cleanup).
* ?String OrderIds are hashed to uint64 via a fast non-cryptographic hash (xxHash or FNV-1a) to avoid string allocations in lookups.
* ?The hash table uses a load factor of 0.7 — when exceeded, a background thread rebuilds into a larger pre-allocated table.
Zero-Allocation Open-Addressing Hash Map
Pre-allocated storage. Linear probing. Tombstone deletion. Zero heap allocation in the hot path.

class="cm">/// <summary>class="cm">/// Zero-allocation, lock-free OrderId ? FsmKey routing table.class="cm">/// Uses open addressing with linear probing.class="cm">/// All storage is pre-allocated at construction.class="cm">/// </summary>class="kw">public sealed unsafe class OrderIdRouter{    class="kw">private class="kw">readonly HashEntry[] _table;    class="kw">private class="kw">readonly int _mask;    class="kw">private class="kw">readonly int _resizeThreshold;    class="kw">private int _count;    class="cm">// Pre-allocated hash computation buffer    class="kw">private class="kw">readonly byte[] _hashBuffer;    class="kw">public OrderIdRouter(int capacity = 65536)    {        class="cm">// Capacity must be power of 2        int actualCapacity = NextPowerOf2(capacity);        _table = class="kw">new HashEntry[actualCapacity];        _mask = actualCapacity - 1;        _resizeThreshold = (int)(actualCapacity * 0.7);        _count = 0;        _hashBuffer = class="kw">new byte[256]; class="cm">// Max OrderId length    }    class="cm">/// <summary>    class="cm">/// Register an OrderId ? FsmKey mapping.    class="cm">/// Lock-free via CAS on the entry's state field.    class="cm">/// </summary>    class="kw">public bool Register(ReadOnlySpan<char> orderId, FsmKey key)    {        class="kw">if (_count >= _resizeThreshold)        {            class="cm">// Trigger async resize — don't block the hot path            TriggerResize();            class="kw">return class="kw">false; class="cm">// Caller should retry        }        ulong hash = ComputeHash(orderId);        int index = (int)(hash & _mask);        int probeCount = 0;        class="kw">while (probeCount < _table.Length)        {            class="kw">ref var entry = class="kw">ref _table[index];            class="cm">// ?? Empty Slot: Try to claim it ???????????????            class="kw">if (entry.State == EntryState.Empty)            {                class="cm">// Write the key first, then CAS the state                entry.Hash = hash;                entry.FsmKey = key;                entry.OrderIdHash = hash; class="cm">// For validation                long expected = (long)EntryState.Empty;                long desired = (long)EntryState.Occupied;                class="kw">if (Interlocked.CompareExchange(                    class="kw">ref entry.State, desired, expected) == expected)                {                    Interlocked.Increment(class="kw">ref _count);                    class="kw">return class="kw">true;                }                class="cm">// CAS failed — another thread claimed it, continue probing            }            class="cm">// ?? Occupied Slot: Check class="kw">for matching hash ????            class="kw">if (entry.State == EntryState.Occupied &&                entry.Hash == hash)            {                class="cm">// Update the FsmKey class="kw">in-place (generation change)                entry.FsmKey = key; class="cm">// Volatile write                class="kw">return class="kw">true;            }            class="cm">// ?? Tombstone Slot: Can reuse ?????????????????            class="kw">if (entry.State == EntryState.Tombstone)            {                long expected = (long)EntryState.Tombstone;                long desired = (long)EntryState.Occupied;                class="kw">if (Interlocked.CompareExchange(                    class="kw">ref entry.State, desired, expected) == expected)                {                    entry.Hash = hash;                    entry.FsmKey = key;                    Interlocked.Increment(class="kw">ref _count);                    class="kw">return class="kw">true;                }            }            class="cm">// ?? Linear Probe ??????????????????????????????            index = (index + 1) & _mask;            probeCount++;        }        class="kw">return class="kw">false; class="cm">// Table full    }    class="cm">/// <summary>    class="cm">/// Resolve an OrderId to its FsmKey.    class="cm">/// Lock-free read — no CAS needed.    class="cm">/// </summary>    class="kw">public FsmKey Resolve(ReadOnlySpan<char> orderId)    {        ulong hash = ComputeHash(orderId);        int index = (int)(hash & _mask);        int probeCount = 0;        class="kw">while (probeCount < _table.Length)        {            class="kw">ref var entry = class="kw">ref _table[index];            class="kw">if (entry.State == EntryState.Empty)                class="kw">return class="kw">default; class="cm">// Not found            class="kw">if (entry.State == EntryState.Occupied &&                entry.Hash == hash)            {                class="kw">return entry.FsmKey;            }            index = (index + 1) & _mask;            probeCount++;        }        class="kw">return class="kw">default;    }    class="cm">/// <summary>    class="cm">/// Unregister an OrderId. Uses tombstone deletion.    class="cm">/// </summary>    class="kw">public class="kw">void Unregister(ReadOnlySpan<char> orderId)    {        ulong hash = ComputeHash(orderId);        int index = (int)(hash & _mask);        int probeCount = 0;        class="kw">while (probeCount < _table.Length)        {            class="kw">ref var entry = class="kw">ref _table[index];            class="kw">if (entry.State == EntryState.Empty) class="kw">return;            class="kw">if (entry.State == EntryState.Occupied &&                entry.Hash == hash)            {                class="cm">// Tombstone deletion                Interlocked.Exchange(                    class="kw">ref entry.State, (long)EntryState.Tombstone);                Interlocked.Decrement(class="kw">ref _count);                class="kw">return;            }            index = (index + 1) & _mask;            probeCount++;        }    }    class="cm">// ?? FNV-1a Hash (Fast, Non-Cryptographic) ?????????????    class="kw">private ulong ComputeHash(ReadOnlySpan<char> orderId)    {        class="kw">const ulong FNV_OFFSET = 14695981039346656037UL;        class="kw">const ulong FNV_PRIME = 1099511628211UL;        ulong hash = FNV_OFFSET;        class="kw">foreach (char c class="kw">in orderId)        {            hash ^= c;            hash *= FNV_PRIME;        }        class="kw">return hash;    }    class="kw">private class="kw">static int NextPowerOf2(int v)    {        v--;        v |= v >> 1; v |= v >> 2;        v |= v >> 4; v |= v >> 8; v |= v >> 16;        class="kw">return v + 1;    }}class="kw">public enum EntryState : long{    Empty = 0,    Occupied = 1,    Tombstone = -1}[StructLayout(LayoutKind.Explicit, Size = 24)]class="kw">public class="kw">struct HashEntry{    [FieldOffset(0)] class="kw">public long State;        class="cm">// 8 bytes    [FieldOffset(8)] class="kw">public ulong Hash;        class="cm">// 8 bytes    [FieldOffset(16)] class="kw">public FsmKey FsmKey;    class="cm">// 8 bytes (int + uint)}
??KEY INSIGHTS
* 1.The HashEntry struct is exactly 24 bytes with explicit layout — no padding waste.
* 2.FNV-1a hash is chosen for speed over cryptographic security. For OrderIds (alphanumeric strings), it provides excellent distribution.
* 3.Tombstone deletion (marking as -1 instead of Empty) preserves probe chain integrity — critical for correctness in open addressing.
* 4.The resize is triggered asynchronously — the hot path never blocks. If resize is in progress, Register returns false and the caller retries.
* 5.ReadOnlySpan<char> avoids string allocation when looking up OrderIds from network buffers.
??
TRAP #5CRITICAL
Missing Circuit Breaker
No global primitive to halt submissions during broker network disconnects, guaranteeing infinite retry loops and queue exhaustion.
??THE TRAP
* •When the broker disconnects, submission failures trigger retries. Without a circuit breaker, retries accumulate exponentially.
* •Each retry allocates memory (callbacks, state objects), eventually causing OOM.
* •The retry storm also masks the real problem — the broker is down — making diagnosis harder.
* •In extreme cases, the retry queue exhausts all available slots, preventing new orders even after the broker recovers.
???THE SOLUTION: Lock-Free Global Submit Circuit Breaker
* ?Implement a three-state circuit breaker (Closed ? Open ? Half-Open) using Interlocked operations.
* ?Closed: Normal operation. Track failure count with Interlocked.Increment.
* ?Open: When failures exceed threshold, halt all submissions. Set a recovery timer.
* ?Half-Open: After recovery timer expires, allow a single "probe" submission. If it succeeds, transition to Closed. If it fails, return to Open.
* ?All state transitions use Interlocked.CompareExchange — no locks, no allocations.
* ?The breaker exposes metrics (failure rate, time in current state) for monitoring dashboards.

Interactive simulation. Click buttons to trigger state transitions.

class="cm">/// <summary>class="cm">/// Lock-free circuit breaker class="kw">for order submissions.class="cm">/// States: Closed ? Open ? Half-Open ? (Closed or Open)class="cm">/// All transitions use Interlocked.CompareExchange.class="cm">/// </summary>class="kw">public sealed class CircuitBreaker : ICircuitBreaker{    class="cm">// ?? Configuration ?????????????????????????????????????    class="kw">private class="kw">readonly int _failureThreshold;    class="kw">private class="kw">readonly TimeSpan _openDuration;    class="kw">private class="kw">readonly int _halfOpenMaxAttempts;    class="cm">// ?? Recovery Timer ????????????????????????????????????    class="kw">private long _openedAtTicks;    class="kw">public CircuitBreaker(        int failureThreshold = 10,        int openDurationSeconds = 30,        int halfOpenMaxAttempts = 3)    {        _failureThreshold = failureThreshold;        _openDuration = TimeSpan.FromSeconds(openDurationSeconds);        _halfOpenMaxAttempts = halfOpenMaxAttempts;        class="cm">// Initialize to Closed state with 0 failures        _packedState = (long)CircuitState.Closed << 16;    }    class="cm">/// <summary>    class="cm">/// Check class="kw">if a submission is allowed.    class="cm">/// Returns class="kw">true class="kw">if the circuit permits the submission.    class="cm">/// </summary>    class="kw">public bool AllowSubmit()    {        long current = Volatile.Read(class="kw">ref _packedState);        var state = (CircuitState)((current >> 16) & 0xFFFF);        class="kw">switch (state)        {            class="kw">case CircuitState.Closed:                class="kw">return class="kw">true;            class="kw">case CircuitState.Open:                class="kw">return TryTransitionToHalfOpen(current);            class="kw">case CircuitState.HalfOpen:                class="kw">return TryAcquireHalfOpenSlot(current);            class="kw">default:                class="kw">return class="kw">false;        }    }    class="cm">/// <summary>    class="cm">/// Record a successful submission result.    class="cm">/// Transitions Half-Open ? Closed on success.    class="cm">/// </summary>    class="kw">public class="kw">void RecordSuccess()    {        long current, desired;        class="kw">do        {            current = Volatile.Read(class="kw">ref _packedState);            var state = (CircuitState)((current >> 16) & 0xFFFF);            class="kw">if (state == CircuitState.HalfOpen)            {                class="cm">// Success class="kw">in Half-Open ? transition to Closed                desired = (long)CircuitState.Closed << 16; class="cm">// Reset failures                class="kw">if (Interlocked.CompareExchange(                    class="kw">ref _packedState, desired, current) == current)                {                    class="kw">return;                }            }            class="kw">else class="kw">if (state == CircuitState.Closed)            {                class="cm">// Reset failure count on success                long resetFailures = current & ~(0xFFFFFFFFL << 32);                class="kw">if (Interlocked.CompareExchange(                    class="kw">ref _packedState, resetFailures, current) == current)                {                    class="kw">return;                }            }            class="kw">else            {                class="kw">return; class="cm">// No action needed class="kw">for Open state            }        } class="kw">while (class="kw">true);    }    class="cm">/// <summary>    class="cm">/// Record a failed submission result.    class="cm">/// Transitions Closed ? Open when threshold is exceeded.    class="cm">/// Transitions Half-Open ? Open on failure.    class="cm">/// </summary>    class="kw">public class="kw">void RecordFailure()    {        long current, desired;        class="kw">do        {            current = Volatile.Read(class="kw">ref _packedState);            var state = (CircuitState)((current >> 16) & 0xFFFF);            int failures = (int)((current >> 32) & 0xFFFFFFFF);            class="kw">switch (state)            {                class="kw">case CircuitState.Closed:                    failures++;                    class="kw">if (failures >= _failureThreshold)                    {                        class="cm">// Threshold exceeded ? Open the circuit                        desired = ((long)CircuitState.Open << 16)                                | ((long)failures << 32);                        class="kw">if (Interlocked.CompareExchange(                            class="kw">ref _packedState, desired, current) == current)                        {                            _openedAtTicks = DateTime.UtcNow.Ticks;                            class="kw">return;                        }                    }                    class="kw">else                    {                        class="cm">// Increment failure count                        desired = current + (1L << 32);                        class="kw">if (Interlocked.CompareExchange(                            class="kw">ref _packedState, desired, current) == current)                        {                            class="kw">return;                        }                    }                    class="kw">break;                class="kw">case CircuitState.HalfOpen:                    class="cm">// Failure class="kw">in Half-Open ? back to Open                    desired = (long)CircuitState.Open << 16;                    class="kw">if (Interlocked.CompareExchange(                        class="kw">ref _packedState, desired, current) == current)                    {                        _openedAtTicks = DateTime.UtcNow.Ticks;                        class="kw">return;                    }                    class="kw">break;                class="kw">default:                    class="kw">return;            }        } class="kw">while (class="kw">true);    }    class="cm">// ?? Internal: Transition Open ? Half-Open ?????????????    class="kw">private bool TryTransitionToHalfOpen(long current)    {        long now = DateTime.UtcNow.Ticks;        class="kw">if (now - _openedAtTicks < _openDuration.Ticks)            class="kw">return class="kw">false; class="cm">// Still class="kw">in open period        long desired = (long)CircuitState.HalfOpen << 16;        class="kw">return Interlocked.CompareExchange(            class="kw">ref _packedState, desired, current) == current;    }    class="cm">// ?? Internal: Acquire a Half-Open probe slot ??????????    class="kw">private bool TryAcquireHalfOpenSlot(long current)    {        int attempts = (int)(current & 0xFFFF);        class="kw">if (attempts >= _halfOpenMaxAttempts)            class="kw">return class="kw">false; class="cm">// Max probe attempts reached        long desired = current + 1; class="cm">// Increment attempt count        class="kw">return Interlocked.CompareExchange(            class="kw">ref _packedState, desired, current) == current;    }    class="cm">// ?? Diagnostics ???????????????????????????????????????    class="kw">public CircuitState CurrentState =>        (CircuitState)((Volatile.Read(class="kw">ref _packedState) >> 16) & 0xFFFF);    class="kw">public int FailureCount =>        (int)((Volatile.Read(class="kw">ref _packedState) >> 32) & 0xFFFFFFFF);    class="kw">public TimeSpan TimeInCurrentState    {        get        {            var state = CurrentState;            class="kw">if (state == CircuitState.Open)            {                class="kw">return TimeSpan.FromTicks(                    DateTime.UtcNow.Ticks - _openedAtTicks);            }            class="kw">return TimeSpan.Zero;        }    }}class="kw">public enum CircuitState : ushort{    Closed = 0,    class="cm">// Normal operation    Open = 1,      class="cm">// Halting submissions    HalfOpen = 2,  class="cm">// Probing class="kw">for recovery}
??KEY INSIGHTS
* 1.The packed state uses 64 bits: 32-bit failure count, 16-bit state enum, 16-bit half-open attempt counter.
* 2.The Open ? Half-Open transition is time-gated by _openedAtTicks — no timer thread needed, just check elapsed time on each AllowSubmit() call.
* 3.Half-Open limits probe attempts to prevent overwhelming a recovering broker. Default is 3 probes.
* 4.Success in Half-Open immediately closes the circuit and resets the failure count.
* 5.The breaker is observable: CurrentState, FailureCount, and TimeInCurrentState can be exposed to monitoring dashboards.
V12 Universal OR Strategy — Build 971 — P3 Architectural Design
All solutions adhere to Zero-Lock and Zero-Allocation DNA constraints


Sonnet 4.6 :

```markdown
# V12 Universal OR Strategy — Architectural Repair Report
**BUILD_TAG**: V12.002 (Build 971)  |  **MODE**: P3 ARCHITECTURAL DESIGN
**REPO**: V12 Universal OR Strategy

---

## ?? TRAPS ADDRESSED

### TRAP-01 — 64-bit Packing Race
**Severity**: CRITICAL
> Generation and State must be updated atomically, requiring 64-bit packing, but 32-bit generations overflow in 4.9 days under high load.

### TRAP-02 — Callback-Only Deadlock (Event Loss Window)
**Severity**: CRITICAL
> Waiting for OnAccountOrderUpdate to map the OrderId creates a 50–500 ms window where async partial-fills drop into the void.

### TRAP-03 — Compound Callback Race
**Severity**: CRITICAL
> If a slot is freed and reallocated before a delayed callback arrives, the callback fails the generation check and the order becomes unmanaged.

### TRAP-04 — ConcurrentDictionary Allocation Violation
**Severity**: HIGH
> Fixing thread-safety of _orderIdToFsmKey using ConcurrentDictionary violates our strict Zero-Allocation hot-path mandate.

### TRAP-05 — Missing Circuit Breaker
**Severity**: CRITICAL
> No global primitive exists to halt submissions during broker network disconnects, guaranteeing infinite retry loops and queue exhaustion.

---

## ??? V12 DNA CONSTRAINTS
- **Zero-Lock Policy**: `lock(stateLock)` is STRICTLY BANNED. Use atomic primitives.
- **Zero-Allocation**: Hot-paths must not allocate on the heap.

---

## Section 1: FIX-01 — FSM State Struct
### 64-bit Atomic Word Packing

**Solves**: TRAP-01

### Overview
We collapse FsmState, Generation, and the Pending flag into a single 64-bit long that can be operated on by Interlocked.CompareExchange. This eliminates any possibility of a torn-read between state fields, which was the root of the 64-bit packing race.

### Key Design Insights
- 16-bit Generation (ushort) placed in bits 32–47 ? natural C# overflow wraps 65535 ? 0 safely, and a slot cannot be recycled 65,536 times during a single in-flight RTT.
- Bit 31 is the Pending flag — a dedicated single-bit check costs zero extra interlocked ops.
- Bits 0–30 hold FsmState — 31 bits gives 2.1 billion distinct state values, far exceeding any realistic FSM.
- All encode/decode helpers are [AggressiveInlining] pure bit-mask operations: zero allocations, no method dispatch.
- The CAS spin loop retries with a fresh observed value on contention — this is the canonical lock-free pattern.

### FsmStateWord.cs — Bit Layout & Atomic Helpers
```csharp
// ???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????
// SECTION 1 — FSM State Struct: 64-bit Atomic Packing
// FILE: V12.Core/FsmStateWord.cs
// ???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????

/// <summary>
/// Packs FSM lifecycle data into a single 64-bit long for use with
/// Interlocked.CompareExchange(ref long, ...). Zero allocations. Lock-free.
///
/// BIT LAYOUT (64 bits total)
/// ???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????
/// ? Bits 63–48 ? Bits 47–32 ?  Bit 31   ? Bits 30–0               ?
/// ?  Reserved  ? Generation ?  Pending  ?  FsmState (enum, 31 vals)?
/// ???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????
///
/// Generation : 16-bit unsigned (0–65535) — wraps ~every 18hrs @ 1M/s
/// Pending    : 1-bit flag — order submitted, awaiting broker OrderId
/// FsmState   : 31-bit enum value space (more than enough for all states)
/// </summary>
internal static class FsmStateWord
{
    // ?? Masks ????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????
    private const long STATE_MASK      = 0x000000007FFFFFFFL; // bits  0–30
    private const long PENDING_MASK    = 0x0000000080000000L; // bit   31
    private const long GENERATION_MASK = 0x0000FFFF00000000L; // bits 32–47
    private const int  GENERATION_SHIFT = 32;
    private const int  GENERATION_BITS  = 16;

    // ?? Encode ???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????
    [MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]
    public static long Encode(FsmState state, ushort generation, bool pending)
    {
        long word = (long)(uint)state;                         // bits  0–30
        if (pending) word |= PENDING_MASK;                     // bit   31
        word |= ((long)generation << GENERATION_SHIFT);        // bits 32–47
        return word;
    }

    // ?? Decode ???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????
    [MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]
    public static FsmState DecodeState(long word)
        => (FsmState)(word & STATE_MASK);

    [MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]
    public static bool DecodePending(long word)
        => (word & PENDING_MASK) != 0;

    [MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]
    public static ushort DecodeGeneration(long word)
        => (ushort)((word >> GENERATION_SHIFT) & 0xFFFF);

    // ?? Generation Increment (wraps safely at ushort.MaxValue) ???????????
    [MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]
    public static ushort NextGeneration(ushort current)
        => (ushort)(current + 1);   // Natural ushort overflow is defined
                                    // and wraps 65535 ? 0 safely.
                                    // Consumers MUST guard with IsSameEpoch().

    // ?? Epoch Guard ??????????????????????????????????????????????????????
    /// <summary>
    /// Two generations are "same epoch" if they are equal.
    /// Wrap-around is safe because a slot cannot be recycled 65536 times
    /// before an in-flight callback completes (network RTT >> slot lifetime).
    /// If ever needed, expand Generation to 32-bit by sacrificing Reserved.
    /// </summary>
    [MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]
    public static bool IsSameEpoch(ushort expected, ushort observed)
        => expected == observed;
}
```

### OrderSlot.cs — CAS Transition Pattern
```csharp
// ?? CAS usage pattern (no locks) ????????????????????????????????????????????
// FILE: V12.Core/OrderSlot.cs  (hot-path transition example)

internal sealed class OrderSlot
{
    private long _stateWord;   // THE only mutable field — 64 bits, aligned

    public bool TryTransition(
        FsmState expectedState,
        FsmState nextState,
        ushort   expectedGeneration,
        bool     clearPending = false)
    {
        long observed = Volatile.Read(ref _stateWord);

        while (true)
        {
            if (FsmStateWord.DecodeState(observed)      != expectedState)      return false;
            if (FsmStateWord.DecodeGeneration(observed) != expectedGeneration) return false;

            bool pendingNow = clearPending
                ? false
                : FsmStateWord.DecodePending(observed);

            long desired = FsmStateWord.Encode(nextState, expectedGeneration, pendingNow);
            long snapshot = Interlocked.CompareExchange(ref _stateWord, desired, observed);

            if (snapshot == observed) return true;  // ? CAS won
            observed = snapshot;                    // ?? retry with fresh value
        }
    }

    /// <summary>Stamp a new generation at slot-recycle time.</summary>
    public void Recycle(ushort newGeneration)
    {
        long fresh = FsmStateWord.Encode(FsmState.Idle, newGeneration, pending: false);
        Volatile.Write(ref _stateWord, fresh);
    }
}
```

### Architect Notes
#### ?? Generation Wrap-Around Contract
> Consumers MUST call IsSameEpoch() before trusting any generation-dependent operation. The wrap is safe provided no callback can survive 65,536 full slot-recycle cycles — a physical impossibility at sub-second RTTs.

#### ? Zero-Lock Guarantee
> TryTransition uses a single Interlocked.CompareExchange. No Monitor, no Mutex, no SemaphoreSlim. The spin is bounded by the number of competing threads, not by I/O.

---

## Section 2: FIX-02 + FIX-03 — Pre-Submit Registration
### Sentinel Lifecycle & Pending Fill Buffer

**Solves**: TRAP-02

### Overview
We eliminate the 50–500 ms OrderId deadlock by registering a CorrelationId sentinel in the zero-alloc map BEFORE the async broker call fires. Any fill events arriving during the Pending window are captured in a fixed-size, wait-free per-slot micro-buffer. On broker ACK, we atomically drain the buffer and clear the Pending flag. This simultaneously defeats TRAP-02 and TRAP-03.

### Key Design Insights
- CorrelationId is a monotonic ulong counter (Interlocked.Increment) — generated locally, never allocated on the heap.
- The sentinel is inserted BEFORE the broker network call. There is no window where a fill can arrive without a valid map entry.
- PendingFillBuffer is a value-type struct (4 unrolled FillEvent fields) — no array, no heap. Capacity 4 is sufficient because RTT << 4 fills per RTT at any realistic throughput.
- TryResolve atomically replaces the sentinel with the real BrokerId in a single logical transaction using the existing zero-alloc map.
- Compound callback race (TRAP-03) is defeated: the generation embedded in the sentinel value is checked on every callback. A recycled slot has a different generation, so stale callbacks are discarded atomically.

### SubmitPipeline.cs — Pre-Submit Registration Flow
```csharp
// ???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????
// SECTION 2 — Pre-Submit Registration: Solving the OrderId Deadlock
// FILE: V12.Core/SubmitPipeline.cs
// ???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????

/// <summary>
/// LIFECYCLE:
///
///  [1] Acquire slot ? set state = Pending (Pending flag = true)
///  [2] Register SENTINEL key in zero-alloc map (BrokerCorrelationId ? slotIndex)
///  [3] Submit to broker async (non-blocking fire-and-forget)
///  [4] Broker callback arrives ? replace sentinel with real OrderId
///  [5] Any fill event arriving BEFORE step 4 hits the sentinel and queues
///      to a per-slot wait-free micro-buffer (see PendingFillBuffer below)
///  [6] On sentinel resolution, drain micro-buffer atomically
/// </summary>
internal static class SubmitPipeline
{
    // Each submission gets a locally-unique correlation id BEFORE network I/O.
    // This is a monotonic counter — wraps safely (ulong, ~584 years @ 1B/s).
    private static ulong _correlationSeed = 0;

    [MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]
    public static ulong NextCorrelationId()
        => Interlocked.Increment(ref _correlationSeed);

    // ?? Step 1-3: Pre-Submit Registration ????????????????????????????????
    public static bool TrySubmit(
        int          slotIndex,
        ushort       generation,
        OrderParams  orderParams,
        IOrderRouter router,
        ZeroAllocMap map)
    {
        // [1] Stamp slot as Pending (atomic — generation unchanged)
        ref OrderSlot slot = ref SlotPool.GetRef(slotIndex);
        if (!slot.TrySetPending(generation)) return false;

        // [2] Register sentinel BEFORE broker call
        ulong correlationId = NextCorrelationId();
        map.RegisterSentinel(correlationId, slotIndex, generation);

        // [3] Fire-and-forget — broker receives correlationId as client tag
        router.SubmitAsync(orderParams, correlationId);   // no await, no alloc
        return true;
    }
}
```

### BrokerCallbackHandler.cs + PendingFillBuffer.cs
```csharp
// ?? Sentinel resolution on OnAccountOrderUpdate callback ?????????????????????
// FILE: V12.Core/BrokerCallbackHandler.cs

internal sealed class BrokerCallbackHandler
{
    private readonly ZeroAllocMap _map;

    // Called by broker adapter on the I/O thread (not our hot-path thread)
    public void OnAccountOrderUpdate(ulong correlationId, long brokerId)
    {
        // Resolve sentinel ? real broker OrderId (lock-free, zero-alloc)
        if (!_map.TryResolve(correlationId, brokerId, out int slotIndex, out ushort gen))
            return;  // Stale or unknown correlation — discard safely

        // Drain the micro-buffer of any fills that arrived during the window
        ref OrderSlot slot = ref SlotPool.GetRef(slotIndex);
        slot.DrainPendingFills(gen);   // processes buffered events atomically

        // Clear the Pending flag — slot now fully active
        slot.TryClearPending(gen);
    }
}

// ?? Per-slot micro-buffer for fills arriving in the Pending window ????????????
// FILE: V12.Core/PendingFillBuffer.cs

/// <summary>
/// A wait-free, fixed-size ring buffer (4 slots) per OrderSlot.
/// Fills arriving during the Pending window are enqueued here.
/// Capacity = 4 is sufficient: broker ACK RTT < 500ms, fill rate << 4/500ms.
/// All fields are value-types — zero heap allocation.
/// </summary>
[StructLayout(LayoutKind.Sequential)]
internal struct PendingFillBuffer
{
    private const int CAPACITY = 4;
    private int  _writeIdx;      // atomic
    private int  _readIdx;       // atomic
    private FillEvent _e0, _e1, _e2, _e3;   // unrolled — no array alloc

    [MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]
    public bool TryEnqueue(in FillEvent ev)
    {
        int w = Interlocked.Increment(ref _writeIdx) - 1;
        if (w - Volatile.Read(ref _readIdx) >= CAPACITY) return false; // overflow guard
        Unsafe.Add(ref _e0, w & (CAPACITY - 1)) = ev;
        return true;
    }

    public void DrainTo(IFillProcessor processor)
    {
        int r = _readIdx;
        int w = Volatile.Read(ref _writeIdx);
        while (r < w)
        {
            processor.Process(in Unsafe.Add(ref _e0, r & (CAPACITY - 1)));
            r++;
        }
        Volatile.Write(ref _readIdx, r);
    }
}
```

### Architect Notes
#### ?? Why CorrelationId and not a pre-allocated BrokerId?
> The broker assigns its own OrderId asynchronously. We cannot know it before submission. The CorrelationId is our local handle — the bridge between our pre-submit world and the broker's post-accept world.

#### ?? Buffer Overflow Guard
> If _writeIdx - _readIdx >= CAPACITY, TryEnqueue returns false. The caller must escalate to a slow-path handler (log + alert). In practice this is unreachable under normal market conditions.

#### ? TRAP-03 Killed at the Root
> Because generation is packed into every map value, a recycled slot with gen+1 will never match the stale callback's embedded gen. The callback is discarded before it can corrupt state.

---

## Section 3: FIX-04 — Zero-Allocation Hash Map
### Open-Addressing Lock-Free Routing Table

**Solves**: TRAP-04

### Overview
ConcurrentDictionary<K,V> allocates buckets, internal nodes, and lock objects on every structural mutation. We replace it with a pre-allocated, open-addressing, linear-probe hash map backed by two primitive arrays. All insertions and lookups are lock-free using CAS on the key array and Volatile writes on the value array.

### Key Design Insights
- Two parallel pre-allocated arrays (ulong[] keys, long[] values) — allocated once at startup, zero runtime heap pressure.
- Open addressing with linear probing: cache-friendly sequential memory access, no pointer chasing.
- Tombstone deletion preserves probe-chain continuity — essential for lock-free correctness without compaction.
- 4096 buckets = 64 KB total (fits in L2 cache). Keep load < 50% ? E[probes] ? 1.5 per operation.
- TryResolve performs the sentinel ? brokerId swap as a two-step Remove + Insert — safe because no other thread can insert the same correlationId (it was unique at generation time).
- Key CAS uses Unsafe.As to reinterpret ulong[] as long[] for Interlocked compatibility without any boxing or additional allocation.

### ZeroAllocMap.cs — Full Lock-Free Implementation
```csharp
// ???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????
// SECTION 3 — Zero-Allocation Lock-Free Routing: ZeroAllocMap
// FILE: V12.Core/ZeroAllocMap.cs
// ???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????

/// <summary>
/// Open-addressing, linear-probe hash map.
/// - Pre-allocated at startup: ZERO runtime heap allocation.
/// - Lock-free reads/writes via Interlocked CAS on each bucket's state word.
/// - Key  : ulong (BrokerId or CorrelationId)
/// - Value: int SlotIndex (21 bits) + ushort Generation (16 bits) packed into long
///
/// CAPACITY: Must be power-of-two. 4096 buckets ? 4 KB.
/// LOAD FACTOR: Keep < 50% for O(1) average probe length.
///   At 50% load: E[probes] ? 1.5  (Knuth's analysis of linear probing)
/// </summary>
internal sealed class ZeroAllocMap
{
    private const int  CAPACITY  = 4096;           // must be power of 2
    private const int  MASK      = CAPACITY - 1;
    private const long EMPTY     = 0L;
    private const long TOMBSTONE = -1L;            // deleted sentinel

    // ?? Bucket layout (128-bit per bucket: key + value, both 64-bit) ?????
    // Stored in two parallel arrays to keep cache-line pressure low on reads.
    private readonly ulong[] _keys   = new ulong[CAPACITY];  // pre-alloc once
    private readonly long[]  _values = new long[CAPACITY];   // pre-alloc once

    // ?? Value packing helpers ?????????????????????????????????????????????
    private const int  SLOT_SHIFT = 16;
    private const long GEN_MASK   = 0xFFFFL;

    [MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]
    private static long PackValue(int slotIndex, ushort gen)
        => ((long)slotIndex << SLOT_SHIFT) | (ushort)gen;

    [MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]
    private static void UnpackValue(long v, out int slotIndex, out ushort gen)
    {
        slotIndex = (int)(v >> SLOT_SHIFT);
        gen = (ushort)(v & GEN_MASK);
    }

    // ?? Insert (called on pre-submit, must be wait-free for writer) ???????
    public bool TryInsert(ulong key, int slotIndex, ushort generation)
    {
        int probe = (int)(key & MASK);
        long newValue = PackValue(slotIndex, generation);

        for (int i = 0; i < CAPACITY; i++, probe = (probe + 1) & MASK)
        {
            ulong existing = Volatile.Read(ref _keys[probe]);
            if (existing != EMPTY && existing != (ulong)TOMBSTONE) continue;

            // CAS the key slot from EMPTY/TOMBSTONE ? key
            ulong expected = existing;
            ulong observed = (ulong)Interlocked.CompareExchange(
                ref Unsafe.As<ulong, long>(ref _keys[probe]),
                (long)key, (long)expected);

            if (observed != expected) { i--; continue; }  // lost race, retry probe

            Volatile.Write(ref _values[probe], newValue);  // value after key is visible
            return true;
        }
        return false; // table full — should never happen at < 50% load
    }

    // ?? Lookup (wait-free single pass for readers) ?????????????????????????
    public bool TryGet(ulong key, out int slotIndex, out ushort generation)
    {
        int probe = (int)(key & MASK);
        slotIndex = 0; generation = 0;

        for (int i = 0; i < CAPACITY; i++, probe = (probe + 1) & MASK)
        {
            ulong k = Volatile.Read(ref _keys[probe]);
            if (k == EMPTY) return false;          // guaranteed empty — stop
            if (k == (ulong)TOMBSTONE) continue;   // deleted — keep probing
            if (k != key) continue;

            long v = Volatile.Read(ref _values[probe]);
            UnpackValue(v, out slotIndex, out generation);
            return true;
        }
        return false;
    }

    // ?? Resolve Sentinel: atomically swap correlationId ? brokerId ?????????
    public bool TryResolve(
        ulong correlationId,
        long  brokerId,
        out int slotIndex,
        out ushort gen)
    {
        slotIndex = 0; gen = 0;
        if (!TryGet(correlationId, out slotIndex, out gen)) return false;

        // Remove old sentinel entry
        TryRemove(correlationId);

        // Insert real broker id under same slot/gen
        TryInsert((ulong)brokerId, slotIndex, gen);
        return true;
    }

    // ?? Remove (mark as tombstone, lock-free) ?????????????????????????????
    public bool TryRemove(ulong key)
    {
        int probe = (int)(key & MASK);
        for (int i = 0; i < CAPACITY; i++, probe = (probe + 1) & MASK)
        {
            ulong k = Volatile.Read(ref _keys[probe]);
            if (k == EMPTY) return false;
            if (k == (ulong)TOMBSTONE) continue;
            if (k != key) continue;

            Volatile.Write(ref _values[probe], TOMBSTONE);
            Interlocked.CompareExchange(
                ref Unsafe.As<ulong, long>(ref _keys[probe]),
                TOMBSTONE, (long)key);
            return true;
        }
        return false;
    }
}
```

### Architect Notes
#### ?? Unsafe.As Usage Contract
> Unsafe.As<ulong, long> is safe here because ulong and long are the same size and alignment. This is a well-known pattern in high-performance .NET. Do not use Unsafe.As across different-size types.

#### ?? Capacity Sizing Formula
> CAPACITY = NextPowerOf2(maxConcurrentOrders × 2). For 1,000 max concurrent orders, use 2048. For 2,000, use 4096. The 50% load-factor headroom is non-negotiable for linear-probe performance.

#### ? Zero Allocation on Hot-Path
> TryInsert, TryGet, and TryRemove touch only the pre-allocated arrays via Volatile and Interlocked. GC pressure is exactly zero. No boxing. No delegates. No closures.

---

## Section 4: FIX-05 — Circuit Breaker
### Lock-Free Global Submit Guard

**Solves**: TRAP-05

### Overview
We implement a 3-state (Closed ? Open ? Half-Open) circuit breaker using only int and long fields operated on by Interlocked primitives. IsSubmitAllowed() is a single branch-predicted Volatile.Read on the Closed path — zero overhead during normal operation. The breaker prevents infinite retry loops and queue exhaustion during broker disconnects.

### Key Design Insights
- State is stored as an int for Interlocked.CompareExchange compatibility. The 3 states are compile-time constants — no enum boxing.
- FAILURE_THRESHOLD consecutive failures (not total) trigger the trip — a single CAS ensures only one thread performs the transition.
- Cooldown uses Environment.TickCount64 (a native OS timer read) — zero allocation, monotonic, 15ms resolution is more than sufficient.
- Half-Open probe is guarded by a separate _probeInflight int CAS — ensures exactly one probe attempt at a time, preventing probe storms.
- RecordSuccess resets _failureCount with a simple Volatile.Write (idempotent — racing resets are harmless since all writers are converging to 0).
- IsSubmitAllowed() is [AggressiveInlining] and returns true in a single Volatile.Read on the Closed fast-path — branch prediction makes this effectively free.

### SubmitCircuitBreaker.cs — Full State Machine
```csharp
// ???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????
// SECTION 4 — Global Submit Circuit Breaker (Lock-Free State Machine)
// FILE: V12.Core/SubmitCircuitBreaker.cs
// ???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????

/// <summary>
/// Lock-free 3-state circuit breaker: Closed ? Open ? Half-Open ? Closed
///
/// STATE TRANSITIONS:
///
///   Closed ??[failures >= THRESHOLD]??? Open
///   Open   ??[cooldown elapsed]??????? Half-Open
///   HalfOpen??[probe succeeds]????????? Closed
///   HalfOpen??[probe fails]???????????? Open
///
/// All state reads and transitions use Interlocked — zero locks, zero alloc.
/// </summary>
internal sealed class SubmitCircuitBreaker
{
    // ?? State enum (stored as int for Interlocked compatibility) ??????????
    private static class BreakerState
    {
        public const int Closed   = 0;   // Normal — submissions allowed
        public const int Open     = 1;   // Tripped — submissions BLOCKED
        public const int HalfOpen = 2;   // Probe — ONE submission allowed
    }

    // ?? Thresholds (tune per deployment) ??????????????????????????????????
    private const int  FAILURE_THRESHOLD   = 5;      // consecutive failures to trip
    private const long COOLDOWN_TICKS      = 30 * TimeSpan.TicksPerSecond; // 30s
    private const int  HALF_OPEN_PROBE_MAX = 1;      // only 1 probe at a time

    // ?? Atomic Fields (all value-type, no heap allocation) ????????????????
    private int  _state          = BreakerState.Closed;
    private int  _failureCount   = 0;
    private long _openTimestamp  = 0L;   // Environment.TickCount64 ticks when Opened
    private int  _probeInflight  = 0;    // guard: only 1 probe at a time

    // ?????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????
    // PUBLIC API
    // ?????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????

    /// <summary>
    /// Returns true if a submission is allowed to proceed.
    /// Called on every hot-path submit attempt — must be allocation-free.
    /// </summary>
    [MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]
    public bool IsSubmitAllowed()
    {
        int state = Volatile.Read(ref _state);

        return state switch
        {
            BreakerState.Closed   => true,
            BreakerState.Open     => TryTransitionToHalfOpen(),
            BreakerState.HalfOpen => TryClaimProbeSlot(),
            _                     => false
        };
    }

    /// <summary>Record a successful broker acknowledgement.</summary>
    [MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]
    public void RecordSuccess()
    {
        // Reset failure counter (non-CAS — idempotent reset is fine)
        Volatile.Write(ref _failureCount, 0);

        int state = Volatile.Read(ref _state);
        if (state == BreakerState.HalfOpen)
        {
            // Probe succeeded — transition back to Closed
            Interlocked.CompareExchange(ref _state, BreakerState.Closed, BreakerState.HalfOpen);
            Volatile.Write(ref _probeInflight, 0);
        }
    }

    /// <summary>Record a broker submission failure (timeout, reject, disconnect).</summary>
    [MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]
    public void RecordFailure()
    {
        int failures = Interlocked.Increment(ref _failureCount);

        if (failures >= FAILURE_THRESHOLD)
        {
            // Only the thread that wins the CAS trips the breaker
            int prev = Interlocked.CompareExchange(
                ref _state, BreakerState.Open, BreakerState.Closed);

            if (prev == BreakerState.Closed)
            {
                // We tripped it — stamp the open time
                Volatile.Write(ref _openTimestamp, Environment.TickCount64);
            }
            else if (prev == BreakerState.HalfOpen)
            {
                // Probe failed — re-trip immediately
                Volatile.Write(ref _openTimestamp, Environment.TickCount64);
                Volatile.Write(ref _probeInflight, 0);
                Volatile.Write(ref _state, BreakerState.Open);
            }
        }
    }

    // ?????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????
    // PRIVATE TRANSITIONS
    // ?????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????

    [MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]
    private bool TryTransitionToHalfOpen()
    {
        long openedAt  = Volatile.Read(ref _openTimestamp);
        long elapsed   = Environment.TickCount64 - openedAt;

        if (elapsed < COOLDOWN_TICKS) return false;   // still cooling down

        // CAS: Open ? HalfOpen (only ONE thread wins)
        int prev = Interlocked.CompareExchange(
            ref _state, BreakerState.HalfOpen, BreakerState.Open);

        if (prev != BreakerState.Open) return false;  // another thread already transitioned

        // Reset probe guard for the new half-open window
        Volatile.Write(ref _probeInflight, 0);
        return TryClaimProbeSlot();
    }

    [MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]
    private bool TryClaimProbeSlot()
    {
        // Atomically claim the single probe slot
        int prev = Interlocked.CompareExchange(ref _probeInflight, 1, 0);
        return prev == 0;  // true = probe slot claimed; false = probe already in-flight
    }
}
```

### OrderEngine.cs — Hot-Path Integration
```csharp
// ?? Integration: Circuit Breaker in the Submit Hot-Path ??????????????????????
// FILE: V12.Core/OrderEngine.cs  (excerpt)

private readonly SubmitCircuitBreaker _breaker = new();

public SubmitResult TrySubmitOrder(OrderParams p)
{
    // ? Check breaker FIRST — zero-alloc, branch-predicted for Closed path
    if (!_breaker.IsSubmitAllowed())
        return SubmitResult.CircuitOpen;

    bool ok = SubmitPipeline.TrySubmit(
        slotIndex: _slotPool.Acquire(),
        generation: _currentGeneration,
        orderParams: p,
        router: _router,
        map: _map);

    if (ok)
        _breaker.RecordSuccess();
    else
        _breaker.RecordFailure();

    return ok ? SubmitResult.Accepted : SubmitResult.BrokerError;
}
```

### Architect Notes
#### ? Fast-Path Cost: One Volatile.Read
> In the Closed state (99.9% of runtime), IsSubmitAllowed() executes exactly one Volatile.Read and one integer comparison. On modern x86-64, this compiles to a single MOV + CMP — sub-nanosecond overhead.

#### ?? Tuning FAILURE_THRESHOLD and COOLDOWN_TICKS
> Set FAILURE_THRESHOLD = 5 and COOLDOWN = 30s as baseline. For HFT environments with < 1ms network SLAs, tighten to THRESHOLD = 3 and COOLDOWN = 10s. Expose as configuration — do not hard-code in production.

#### ?? No Automatic Reconnect Logic Here
> The circuit breaker only controls submission gating. Broker reconnect/re-subscribe logic must live in a separate infrastructure layer that calls RecordSuccess() upon confirmed reconnection.

| TRAP-02 | CRITICAL | FIX-02 | Pre-submit CorrelationId sentinel + PendingFillBuffer |
