END OF V12 ARCHITECTURAL REPAIR REPORT
BUILD 971 | P3 ARCHITECTURAL DESIGN | ZERO-LOCK | ZERO-ALLOC

Qwen 3.6 plus preview:

???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????
  V12 UNIVERSAL OR STRATEGY — ARCHITECTURAL REPAIR REPORT
  V12.002 (Build 971) | P3 Architectural Design
???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????

???  V12 DNA CONSTRAINTS
???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????
  ?? Zero-Lock Policy: lock(stateLock) is STRICTLY BANNED. All synchronization via Interlocked primitives.
  ?? Zero-Allocation: Hot-paths must not allocate on the heap. All structures pre-allocated at startup.

?? EXECUTIVE SUMMARY
???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????
  Total Traps Identified: 5
  Critical: 3 | High: 2
  Status: DESIGNED

  Our adversarial review identified 5 catastrophic traps in the
  lock-free order management architecture. This report defines the
  implementation patterns that resolve each trap while strictly
  adhering to the V12 DNA constraints: Zero-Lock and Zero-Allocation
  in all hot paths.

???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????
  TRAP #1: The 64-bit Packing Race
  Severity: CRITICAL
???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????

?? THE TRAP
???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????
  Generation and State must be updated atomically, requiring 64-bit packing, but 32-bit generations overflow in 4.9 days under high load.

  1. The FSM slot state and a generation counter are stored in separate fields.
  2. Updating them separately creates a TOCTOU race: Thread A reads state=Active, Thread B frees the slot and increments generation, Thread A writes state=Free — corrupting the new occupant's state.
  3. Using Interlocked.CompareExchange on a single 64-bit value solves the atomicity, but packing requires careful bit allocation.
  4. A naive 32-bit generation counter wraps in ~4.9 days at 10K ops/sec, causing ABA problems where old callbacks match new slots.

???  THE SOLUTION: Packed 64-bit FSM State with Safe Generation Wrap-Around
???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????
  1. Pack State (16 bits), Generation (32 bits), and a Pending flag (1 bit) into a single 64-bit long.
  2. Use Interlocked.CompareExchange for all state transitions — this is the ONLY way to guarantee atomicity.
  3. Handle 32-bit wrap-around by treating generation as a monotonic counter that wraps to 1 (never 0) and using a "generation gap" check to detect ABA.
  4. The Pending flag (bit 63) allows pre-registration of OrderIds before broker submission completes.
  5. Remaining 15 bits are reserved for future expansion (circuit breaker slot flags, etc.).

?? FsmPackedState.cs — The Core Packed State Struct ?????????????????????????????????????????
?
?  /// <summary>
?  /// 64-bit packed FSM state for lock-free atomic operations.
?  /// Layout: [63:48] Reserved(15) | [47:16] Generation(32) | [15:1] State(15) | [0] Pending(1)
?  /// All mutations MUST use Interlocked.CompareExchange on the full 64-bit value.
?  /// </summary>
?  [StructLayout(LayoutKind.Sequential, Size = 8)]
?  public readonly struct FsmPackedState : IEquatable<FsmPackedState>
?  {
?      private readonly long _value;
?  
?      // ?? Bit Layout Constants ??????????????????????????????
?      private const int PENDING_SHIFT    = 0;
?      private const long PENDING_MASK    = 0x0000_0000_0000_0001L;
?  
?      private const int STATE_SHIFT      = 1;
?      private const int STATE_BITS       = 15;
?      private const long STATE_MASK      = 0x0000_0000_0000_7FFEL; // bits 1-15
?  
?      private const int GENERATION_SHIFT = 16;
?      private const long GENERATION_MASK = 0x0000_FFFF_FFFF_0000L; // bits 16-47
?  
?      private const int RESERVED_SHIFT   = 48;
?      private const long RESERVED_MASK   = 0xFFFF_0000_0000_0000L; // bits 48-63
?  
?      // ?? Generation Constants ??????????????????????????????
?      private const uint GEN_MAX         = 0xFFFF_FFFFu;
?      private const uint GEN_WRAP_TARGET = 1; // Never wrap to 0
?  
?      // ?? Factory Methods ???????????????????????????????????
?      public static FsmPackedState Create(
?          FsmState state,
?          uint generation,
?          bool pending = false)
?      {
?          long value = 0;
?          value |= ((long)state & STATE_MASK);
?          value |= ((long)generation << GENERATION_SHIFT) & GENERATION_MASK;
?          if (pending) value |= PENDING_MASK;
?          return new FsmPackedState(value);
?      }
?  
?      public static FsmPackedState Empty => new(0);
?  
?      // ?? Property Accessors (Zero-Alloc, Inlined) ??????????
?      [MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]
?      public FsmState State => (FsmState)(_value & STATE_MASK);
?  
?      [MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]
?      public uint Generation => (uint)((_value & GENERATION_MASK) >> GENERATION_SHIFT);
?  
?      [MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]
?      public bool IsPending => (_value & PENDING_MASK) != 0;
?  
?      [MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]
?      public bool IsValid => _value != 0;
?  
?      // ?? Atomic Transition: CAS Loop ???????????????????????
?      /// <summary>
?      /// Atomically transitions from expectedState to newState.
?      /// Returns true if the transition succeeded.
?      /// Generation is incremented on every successful transition
?      /// to prevent ABA problems.
?      /// </summary>
?      [MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]
?      public static bool TryTransition(
?          ref long slot,
?          FsmPackedState expected,
?          FsmState newState,
?          out FsmPackedState committed)
?      {
?          long current, desired;
?          int spins = 0;
?  
?          do
?          {
?              current = Volatile.Read(ref slot);
?  
?              // ?? Optimistic Check ??????????????????????????
?              if (current != expected._value)
?              {
?                  committed = new FsmPackedState(current);
?                  return false;
?              }
?  
?              // ?? Build Desired Value ???????????????????????
?              uint currentGen = (uint)((current & GENERATION_MASK) >> GENERATION_SHIFT);
?              uint nextGen = IncrementGeneration(currentGen);
?  
?              desired = current & RESERVED_MASK; // preserve reserved
?              desired |= ((long)newState & STATE_MASK);
?              desired |= ((long)nextGen << GENERATION_SHIFT) & GENERATION_MASK;
?  
?              spins++;
?          }
?          while (Interlocked.CompareExchange(ref slot, desired, current) != current);
?  
?          committed = new FsmPackedState(desired);
?          return true;
?      }
?  
?      // ?? Safe Generation Increment with Wrap Detection ?????
?      [MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]
?      private static uint IncrementGeneration(uint current)
?      {
?          if (current >= GEN_MAX)
?          {
?              // WRAP DETECTION: Jump to GEN_WRAP_TARGET (1) instead of 0.
?              // This creates a "generation gap" — any callback carrying
?              // generation 0 will never match a slot at generation 1.
?              // At 10K ops/sec, 32-bit wrap takes ~4.9 days.
?              // The gap ensures old callbacks from the previous cycle
?              // are definitively rejected.
?              return GEN_WRAP_TARGET;
?          }
?          return current + 1;
?      }
?  
?      // ?? Generation Gap Validation ?????????????????????????
?      /// <summary>
?      /// Validates that a callback's generation matches the slot's
?      /// current generation, accounting for wrap-around.
?      /// Returns false if the callback is from a previous generation cycle.
?      /// </summary>
?      [MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]
?      public static bool ValidateGeneration(
?          uint callbackGeneration,
?          uint slotGeneration)
?      {
?          if (callbackGeneration == slotGeneration) return true;
?  
?          // Detect wrap-around mismatch:
?          // If slot is in a new cycle (gen < callbackGen) and
?          // the gap is small, it might be a legitimate wrap.
?          // If the gap is large, it's a stale callback.
?          if (slotGeneration < callbackGeneration)
?          {
?              // Slot wrapped, callback is from previous cycle
?              // The gap between GEN_MAX and GEN_WRAP_TARGET = 1
?              // ensures this is always detected as stale.
?              return false;
?          }
?  
?          // Normal case: callback is behind slot (stale)
?          return false;
?      }
?  
?      // ?? IEquatable ????????????????????????????????????????
?      public bool Equals(FsmPackedState other) => _value == other._value;
?      public override bool Equals(object? obj) => obj is FsmPackedState s && Equals(s);
?      public override int GetHashCode() => _value.GetHashCode();
?      public override string ToString() =>
?          $"State={State} Gen={Generation} Pending={IsPending}";
?  }
?
?????????????????????????????????????????????????????????

?? FsmState.cs — State Enum Definition ?????????????????????????????????????????
?
?  /// <summary>
?  /// FSM states for order lifecycle management.
?  /// Values must fit within 15 bits (max value: 32767).
?  /// </summary>
?  public enum FsmState : ushort
?  {
?      /// <summary>Slot is free and available for allocation.</summary>
?      Free        = 0,
?  
?      /// <summary>Order registered, pending broker submission.</summary>
?      Pending     = 1,
?  
?      /// <summary>Order submitted to broker, awaiting acknowledgment.</summary>
?      Submitted   = 2,
?  
?      /// <summary>Order acknowledged by broker, actively managed.</summary>
?      Active      = 3,
?  
?      /// <summary>Order partially filled, awaiting remaining fills.</summary>
?      PartialFill = 4,
?  
?      /// <summary>Order fully filled — terminal state.</summary>
?      Filled      = 5,
?  
?      /// <summary>Order cancelled — terminal state.</summary>
?      Cancelled   = 6,
?  
?      /// <summary>Order rejected by broker — terminal state.</summary>
?      Rejected    = 7,
?  
?      /// <summary>Order expired (TTL exceeded) — terminal state.</summary>
?      Expired     = 8,
?  
?      /// <summary>Order in cancellation process (awaiting broker confirm).</summary>
?      Cancelling  = 9,
?  }
?
?????????????????????????????????????????????????????????

?? KEY INSIGHTS
???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????
  1. All state transitions go through TryTransition() — no direct field writes allowed.
  2. Generation increments on EVERY transition, not just slot reuse. This makes every state change uniquely identifiable.
  3. The wrap-to-1 (never 0) strategy creates a definitive generation gap. A callback with gen=0x00000000 can never match a slot at gen=0x00000001.
  4. Reserved bits (48-63) are future-proofing: circuit breaker flags, priority hints, or debug markers can be added without changing the struct layout.
  5. The CAS loop includes a spin counter for diagnostics — if spins > 10, log a contention warning.

???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????
  TRAP #2: Callback-Only Deadlock (Event Loss Window)
  Severity: CRITICAL
???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????

?? THE TRAP
???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????
  Waiting for OnAccountOrderUpdate to map the OrderId creates a 50-500ms window where async partial-fills drop into the void.

  1. Current flow: Submit order ? wait for broker ack ? OnAccountOrderUpdate fires ? map OrderId to FsmKey ? begin managing fills.
  2. The 50-500ms gap between submission and callback is the "Event Loss Window" — any partial fills arriving in this window have no FsmKey to route to.
  3. Under high-frequency trading conditions, partial fills can arrive within milliseconds of submission.
  4. Lost fills = lost money. This is not a theoretical concern.

???  THE SOLUTION: Pre-Submit Registration with Pending State
???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????
  1. Register the OrderId-to-FsmKey mapping BEFORE the async broker call, using the Pending flag in the packed state.
  2. The flow becomes: Allocate slot ? Set state=Pending ? Register OrderId ? Submit to broker ? On callback, transition Pending?Submitted?Active.
  3. The Pending flag (bit 0) acts as a "do not execute" marker — callbacks that arrive during this window are queued, not dropped.
  4. A lock-free pending queue buffers early fills until the OrderId mapping is confirmed.
  5. If the broker submission fails, the slot is atomically transitioned back to Free and the OrderId mapping is removed.

?? OrderSubmitter.cs — Pre-Submit Registration Flow ?????????????????????????????????????????
?
?  public unsafe class OrderSubmitter
?  {
?      private readonly SlotAllocator _slots;
?      private readonly OrderIdRouter _router;
?      private readonly PendingFillQueue _pendingQueue;
?      private readonly ICircuitBreaker _circuitBreaker;
?  
?      /// <summary>
?      /// SUBMIT FLOW: Zero-dead, pre-registered submission.
?      /// The OrderId is mapped BEFORE the async broker call.
?      /// </summary>
?      public SubmitResult Submit(NewOrderRequest request)
?      {
?          // ?? Step 0: Circuit Breaker Check ?????????????????
?          if (!_circuitBreaker.AllowSubmit())
?              return SubmitResult.CircuitOpen;
?  
?          // ?? Step 1: Allocate a free slot ??????????????????
?          int slotIndex = _slots.Allocate();
?          if (slotIndex < 0)
?              return SubmitResult.NoSlotsAvailable;
?  
?          ref var slot = ref _slots.GetSlot(slotIndex);
?          uint generation = slot.State.Generation + 1;
?  
?          // ?? Step 2: PRE-REGISTER with Pending flag ????????
?          // This is the CRITICAL step that eliminates the
?          // Event Loss Window. The OrderId is mapped NOW,
?          // before any network I/O.
?          var pendingState = FsmPackedState.Create(
?              FsmState.Pending, generation, pending: true);
?  
?          slot.StateValue = pendingState._value; // atomic write
?          // ^^^ State is Pending, so callbacks know to queue
?  
?          // ?? Step 3: Register OrderId ? FsmKey mapping ?????
?          var fsmKey = new FsmKey(slotIndex, generation);
?          _router.Register(request.ClientOrderId, fsmKey);
?  
?          // ?? Step 4: Submit to broker (async, non-blocking) ?
?          try
?          {
?              _broker.SubmitAsync(request, OnBrokerAck, OnBrokerReject);
?              return SubmitResult.Accepted;
?          }
?          catch
?          {
?              // ?? Step 5: Rollback on submission failure ?????
?              RollbackSubmission(slotIndex, generation);
?              return SubmitResult.SubmissionFailed;
?          }
?      }
?  
?      /// <summary>
?      /// CALLBACK: Broker acknowledged the order.
?      /// Transition from Pending ? Submitted ? Active.
?      /// </summary>
?      private void OnBrokerAck(BrokerAck ack)
?      {
?          var fsmKey = _router.Resolve(ack.ClientOrderId);
?          if (fsmKey == default) return; // Should not happen
?  
?          ref var slot = ref _slots.GetSlot(fsmKey.SlotIndex);
?  
?          // Validate generation — reject stale callbacks
?          if (!FsmPackedState.ValidateGeneration(
?              fsmKey.Generation, slot.State.Generation))
?          {
?              _router.Unregister(ack.ClientOrderId);
?              return;
?          }
?  
?          // ?? Atomic transition: Pending ? Submitted ????????
?          var expected = FsmPackedState.Create(
?              FsmState.Pending, fsmKey.Generation, pending: true);
?  
?          if (FsmPackedState.TryTransition(
?              ref slot.StateValue, expected, FsmState.Submitted, out _))
?          {
?              // ?? Process any buffered pending fills ?????????
?              _pendingQueue.Drain(ack.ClientOrderId, ProcessFill);
?  
?              // ?? Transition to Active ??????????????????????
?              FsmPackedState.TryTransition(
?                  ref slot.StateValue,
?                  FsmPackedState.Create(FsmState.Submitted, fsmKey.Generation + 1),
?                  FsmState.Active,
?                  out _);
?          }
?      }
?  
?      private void RollbackSubmission(int slotIndex, uint generation)
?      {
?          ref var slot = ref _slots.GetSlot(slotIndex);
?          var expected = FsmPackedState.Create(
?              FsmState.Pending, generation, pending: true);
?  
?          if (FsmPackedState.TryTransition(
?              ref slot.StateValue, expected, FsmState.Free, out _))
?          {
?              _slots.Free(slotIndex);
?          }
?      }
?  }
?
?????????????????????????????????????????????????????????

?? PendingFillQueue.cs — Lock-Free Early Fill Buffer ?????????????????????????????????????????
?
?  /// <summary>
?  /// Lock-free ring buffer for fills that arrive before the
?  /// OrderId mapping is confirmed (during the Pending window).
?  /// Pre-allocated — zero heap allocation in the hot path.
?  /// </summary>
?  public sealed class PendingFillQueue
?  {
?      private readonly FillEntry[] _buffer;
?      private readonly int _mask;
?      private long _head; // CAS-updated
?      private long _tail; // CAS-updated
?  
?      public PendingFillQueue(int capacity = 1024)
?      {
?          // Capacity must be power of 2 for mask-based indexing
?          _buffer = new FillEntry[capacity];
?          _mask = capacity - 1;
?          _head = 0;
?          _tail = 0;
?      }
?  
?      /// <summary>
?      /// Enqueue a fill event. Returns false if queue is full.
?      /// </summary>
?      public bool Enqueue(FillEvent fill)
?      {
?          long tail, head, next;
?          do
?          {
?              tail = Volatile.Read(ref _tail);
?              head = Volatile.Read(ref _head);
?              next = tail + 1;
?  
?              if (next - head > _mask) return false; // Full
?          }
?          while (Interlocked.CompareExchange(ref _tail, next, tail) != tail);
?  
?          _buffer[tail & _mask] = fill;
?          return true;
?      }
?  
?      /// <summary>
?      /// Drain all fills for a specific OrderId and process them.
?      /// Called when the OrderId mapping is confirmed.
?      /// </summary>
?      public void Drain(string orderId, Action<FillEvent> processor)
?      {
?          long head = Volatile.Read(ref _head);
?          long tail = Volatile.Read(ref _tail);
?  
?          for (long i = head; i < tail; i++)
?          {
?              ref var entry = ref _buffer[i & _mask];
?              if (entry.OrderId == orderId)
?              {
?                  processor(entry.Fill);
?                  entry = default; // Clear after processing
?                  Volatile.Write(ref _head, i + 1);
?              }
?          }
?      }
?  }
?
?????????????????????????????????????????????????????????

?? KEY INSIGHTS
???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????
  1. The Pending flag is the key innovation — it marks slots as "registered but not yet confirmed," allowing the router to accept callbacks while deferring execution.
  2. The PendingFillQueue is a bounded SPSC ring buffer — single producer (callback thread), single consumer (ack handler). No locks needed.
  3. Rollback on failure is atomic: the CAS ensures we only free the slot if it's still in the Pending state with the expected generation.
  4. This eliminates the 50-500ms Event Loss Window entirely — fills are either processed immediately or buffered, never dropped.

???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????
  TRAP #3: Compound Callback Race
  Severity: HIGH
???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????

?? THE TRAP
???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????
  If a slot is freed and reallocated before a delayed callback arrives, the callback fails the generation check and the order becomes unmanaged.

  1. Thread A frees slot 42 (generation 5). Thread B allocates slot 42 (generation 6). A delayed callback for generation 5 arrives.
  2. The generation check correctly rejects the callback — but now the order from generation 5 is permanently unmanaged.
  3. This is a correctness issue: the order's state is unknown, fills are lost, and risk management is compromised.
  4. The root cause is that freeing a slot destroys the order's identity before all callbacks have been processed.

???  THE SOLUTION: Graceful Callback Degradation with Tombstone Routing
???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????
  1. When a callback fails the generation check, instead of silently dropping it, route it to a "tombstone" handler.
  2. The tombstone handler logs the orphaned event and attempts recovery via the OrderId (which remains valid even if the slot is reused).
  3. Implement a "delayed free" mechanism: slots enter a Tombstone state for a configurable grace period (e.g., 30 seconds) before becoming truly Free.
  4. During the Tombstone state, the OrderId mapping is preserved but the slot cannot be reallocated.
  5. A background sweeper transitions Tombstone slots to Free after the grace period expires.

?? CallbackHandler.cs — Generation-Aware Callback Routing ?????????????????????????????????????????
?
?  public sealed class CallbackHandler
?  {
?      private readonly SlotAllocator _slots;
?      private readonly OrderIdRouter _router;
?      private readonly TombstoneRegistry _tombstones;
?  
?      /// <summary>
?      /// Handle an incoming fill/cancel/ack callback.
?      /// Uses generation check + tombstone fallback for safety.
?      /// </summary>
?      public void HandleCallback(CallbackEvent evt)
?      {
?          var fsmKey = _router.Resolve(evt.OrderId);
?          if (fsmKey == default)
?          {
?              // OrderId not found — check tombstones
?              HandleTombstoneCallback(evt);
?              return;
?          }
?  
?          ref var slot = ref _slots.GetSlot(fsmKey.SlotIndex);
?          long currentState = Volatile.Read(ref slot.StateValue);
?          var state = new FsmPackedState(currentState);
?  
?          // ?? Generation Check ??????????????????????????????
?          if (fsmKey.Generation != state.Generation)
?          {
?              // GENERATION MISMATCH: Slot was reused.
?              // Route to tombstone handler for recovery.
?              HandleTombstoneCallback(evt);
?              return;
?          }
?  
?          // ?? Pending Check ?????????????????????????????????
?          if (state.IsPending)
?          {
?              // Slot is in Pending state — buffer the fill
?              // until the broker ack confirms the mapping.
?              _pendingQueue.Enqueue(new FillEvent
?              {
?                  OrderId = evt.OrderId,
?                  Fill = evt.Fill
?              });
?              return;
?          }
?  
?          // ?? Process the callback ??????????????????????????
?          ProcessCallback(fsmKey, evt, ref slot);
?      }
?  
?      /// <summary>
?      /// Handle callbacks for orders whose slots have been reused.
?      /// Attempts recovery via the OrderId and logs for audit.
?      /// </summary>
?      private void HandleTombstoneCallback(CallbackEvent evt)
?      {
?          var tombstone = _tombstones.Lookup(evt.OrderId);
?          if (tombstone != null)
?          {
?              // Found tombstone — process via recovery path
?              tombstone.Recover(evt);
?          }
?          else
?          {
?              // No tombstone — this is a genuine orphan.
?              // Log at WARN level for audit trail.
?              _logger.Warn(
?                  "ORPHAN_CALLBACK: OrderId={OrderId} " +
?                  "Type={Type} — no slot, no tombstone",
?                  evt.OrderId, evt.Type);
?          }
?      }
?  }
?
?????????????????????????????????????????????????????????

?? TombstoneRegistry.cs — Delayed Free Mechanism ?????????????????????????????????????????
?
?  /// <summary>
?  /// Manages tombstone entries for slots that have been freed
?  /// but may still receive delayed callbacks.
?  /// Pre-allocated array — zero allocation in hot path.
?  /// </summary>
?  public sealed class TombstoneRegistry
?  {
?      private readonly TombstoneEntry[] _entries;
?      private readonly long _gracePeriodTicks;
?      private int _count;
?  
?      public TombstoneRegistry(int capacity, TimeSpan gracePeriod)
?      {
?          _entries = new TombstoneEntry[capacity];
?          _gracePeriodTicks = gracePeriod.Ticks;
?          _count = 0;
?      }
?  
?      /// <summary>
?      /// Register a tombstone when a slot is freed.
?      /// The OrderId mapping is preserved for the grace period.
?      /// </summary>
?      public void Register(string orderId, FsmKey key, OrderSnapshot snapshot)
?      {
?          int index = Interlocked.Increment(ref _count) - 1;
?          if (index >= _entries.Length)
?          {
?              // Registry full — log and skip
?              // (This should never happen with proper capacity)
?              return;
?          }
?  
?          _entries[index] = new TombstoneEntry
?          {
?              OrderId = orderId,
?              Key = key,
?              Snapshot = snapshot,
?              ExpiresAt = DateTime.UtcNow.Ticks + _gracePeriodTicks,
?              IsActive = true
?          };
?      }
?  
?      public TombstoneEntry? Lookup(string orderId)
?      {
?          for (int i = 0; i < _count; i++)
?          {
?              ref var entry = ref _entries[i];
?              if (entry.IsActive && entry.OrderId == orderId)
?              {
?                  if (DateTime.UtcNow.Ticks > entry.ExpiresAt)
?                  {
?                      entry.IsActive = false; // Expired
?                      return null;
?                  }
?                  return entry;
?              }
?          }
?          return null;
?      }
?  
?      /// <summary>
?      /// Sweep expired tombstones. Call periodically from
?      /// a background thread (not in the hot path).
?      /// </summary>
?      public void Sweep()
?      {
?          long now = DateTime.UtcNow.Ticks;
?          for (int i = 0; i < _count; i++)
?          {
?              if (_entries[i].IsActive && now > _entries[i].ExpiresAt)
?              {
?                  _entries[i].IsActive = false;
?              }
?          }
?      }
?  }
?
?????????????????????????????????????????????????????????

?? KEY INSIGHTS
???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????
  1. The tombstone pattern trades a small amount of memory (pre-allocated array) for correctness — no order is ever silently lost.
  2. The grace period should be tuned to your broker's maximum callback latency. Start with 30s and measure.
  3. The OrderIdRouter mapping is NOT removed when a slot is freed — it remains valid until the tombstone expires.
  4. The Sweep() method runs on a background timer, not in the hot path. It's O(n) but n is bounded by the tombstone capacity.

???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????
  TRAP #4: ConcurrentDictionary Allocation Violation
  Severity: HIGH
???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????

?? THE TRAP
???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????
  Fixing the thread-safety of _orderIdToFsmKey using ConcurrentDictionary violates our strict Zero-Allocation hot-path mandate.

  1. ConcurrentDictionary<TKey, TValue> allocates Node objects, bucket arrays, and lock objects on every insertion.
  2. Under high-frequency order flow (10K+ orders/sec), this generates megabytes of garbage per second.
  3. GC pauses of even 1ms can cause missed market opportunities and slippage.
  4. The hot path (order submission + callback routing) must be zero-allocation.

???  THE SOLUTION: Lock-Free Open Addressing Hash Map with Pre-Allocated Storage
???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????
  1. Replace ConcurrentDictionary with a pre-allocated open-addressing hash table using linear probing.
  2. All storage is allocated once at startup — zero heap allocation during operation.
  3. Use Interlocked.CompareExchange for lock-free insertions and a two-phase deletion (tombstone marker + background cleanup).
  4. String OrderIds are hashed to uint64 via a fast non-cryptographic hash (xxHash or FNV-1a) to avoid string allocations in lookups.
  5. The hash table uses a load factor of 0.7 — when exceeded, a background thread rebuilds into a larger pre-allocated table.

?? OrderIdRouter.cs — Zero-Allocation Lock-Free Hash Map ?????????????????????????????????????????
?
?  /// <summary>
?  /// Zero-allocation, lock-free OrderId ? FsmKey routing table.
?  /// Uses open addressing with linear probing.
?  /// All storage is pre-allocated at construction.
?  /// </summary>
?  public sealed unsafe class OrderIdRouter
?  {
?      private readonly HashEntry[] _table;
?      private readonly int _mask;
?      private readonly int _resizeThreshold;
?      private int _count;
?  
?      // Pre-allocated hash computation buffer
?      private readonly byte[] _hashBuffer;
?  
?      public OrderIdRouter(int capacity = 65536)
?      {
?          // Capacity must be power of 2
?          int actualCapacity = NextPowerOf2(capacity);
?          _table = new HashEntry[actualCapacity];
?          _mask = actualCapacity - 1;
?          _resizeThreshold = (int)(actualCapacity * 0.7);
?          _count = 0;
?          _hashBuffer = new byte[256]; // Max OrderId length
?      }
?  
?      /// <summary>
?      /// Register an OrderId ? FsmKey mapping.
?      /// Lock-free via CAS on the entry's state field.
?      /// </summary>
?      public bool Register(ReadOnlySpan<char> orderId, FsmKey key)
?      {
?          if (_count >= _resizeThreshold)
?          {
?              // Trigger async resize — don't block the hot path
?              TriggerResize();
?              return false; // Caller should retry
?          }
?  
?          ulong hash = ComputeHash(orderId);
?          int index = (int)(hash & _mask);
?          int probeCount = 0;
?  
?          while (probeCount < _table.Length)
?          {
?              ref var entry = ref _table[index];
?  
?              // ?? Empty Slot: Try to claim it ???????????????
?              if (entry.State == EntryState.Empty)
?              {
?                  // Write the key first, then CAS the state
?                  entry.Hash = hash;
?                  entry.FsmKey = key;
?                  entry.OrderIdHash = hash; // For validation
?  
?                  long expected = (long)EntryState.Empty;
?                  long desired = (long)EntryState.Occupied;
?  
?                  if (Interlocked.CompareExchange(
?                      ref entry.State, desired, expected) == expected)
?                  {
?                      Interlocked.Increment(ref _count);
?                      return true;
?                  }
?                  // CAS failed — another thread claimed it, continue probing
?              }
?  
?              // ?? Occupied Slot: Check for matching hash ????
?              if (entry.State == EntryState.Occupied &&
?                  entry.Hash == hash)
?              {
?                  // Update the FsmKey in-place (generation change)
?                  entry.FsmKey = key; // Volatile write
?                  return true;
?              }
?  
?              // ?? Tombstone Slot: Can reuse ?????????????????
?              if (entry.State == EntryState.Tombstone)
?              {
?                  long expected = (long)EntryState.Tombstone;
?                  long desired = (long)EntryState.Occupied;
?  
?                  if (Interlocked.CompareExchange(
?                      ref entry.State, desired, expected) == expected)
?                  {
?                      entry.Hash = hash;
?                      entry.FsmKey = key;
?                      Interlocked.Increment(ref _count);
?                      return true;
?                  }
?              }
?  
?              // ?? Linear Probe ??????????????????????????????
?              index = (index + 1) & _mask;
?              probeCount++;
?          }
?  
?          return false; // Table full
?      }
?  
?      /// <summary>
?      /// Resolve an OrderId to its FsmKey.
?      /// Lock-free read — no CAS needed.
?      /// </summary>
?      public FsmKey Resolve(ReadOnlySpan<char> orderId)
?      {
?          ulong hash = ComputeHash(orderId);
?          int index = (int)(hash & _mask);
?          int probeCount = 0;
?  
?          while (probeCount < _table.Length)
?          {
?              ref var entry = ref _table[index];
?  
?              if (entry.State == EntryState.Empty)
?                  return default; // Not found
?  
?              if (entry.State == EntryState.Occupied &&
?                  entry.Hash == hash)
?              {
?                  return entry.FsmKey;
?              }
?  
?              index = (index + 1) & _mask;
?              probeCount++;
?          }
?  
?          return default;
?      }
?  
?      /// <summary>
?      /// Unregister an OrderId. Uses tombstone deletion.
?      /// </summary>
?      public void Unregister(ReadOnlySpan<char> orderId)
?      {
?          ulong hash = ComputeHash(orderId);
?          int index = (int)(hash & _mask);
?          int probeCount = 0;
?  
?          while (probeCount < _table.Length)
?          {
?              ref var entry = ref _table[index];
?  
?              if (entry.State == EntryState.Empty) return;
?  
?              if (entry.State == EntryState.Occupied &&
?                  entry.Hash == hash)
?              {
?                  // Tombstone deletion
?                  Interlocked.Exchange(
?                      ref entry.State, (long)EntryState.Tombstone);
?                  Interlocked.Decrement(ref _count);
?                  return;
?              }
?  
?              index = (index + 1) & _mask;
?              probeCount++;
?          }
?      }
?  
?      // ?? FNV-1a Hash (Fast, Non-Cryptographic) ?????????????
?      private ulong ComputeHash(ReadOnlySpan<char> orderId)
?      {
?          const ulong FNV_OFFSET = 14695981039346656037UL;
?          const ulong FNV_PRIME = 1099511628211UL;
?  
?          ulong hash = FNV_OFFSET;
?          foreach (char c in orderId)
?          {
?              hash ^= c;
?              hash *= FNV_PRIME;
?          }
?          return hash;
?      }
?  
?      private static int NextPowerOf2(int v)
?      {
?          v--;
?          v |= v >> 1; v |= v >> 2;
?          v |= v >> 4; v |= v >> 8; v |= v >> 16;
?          return v + 1;
?      }
?  }
?  
?  public enum EntryState : long
?  {
?      Empty = 0,
?      Occupied = 1,
?      Tombstone = -1
?  }
?  
?  [StructLayout(LayoutKind.Explicit, Size = 24)]
?  public struct HashEntry
?  {
?      [FieldOffset(0)] public long State;        // 8 bytes
?      [FieldOffset(8)] public ulong Hash;        // 8 bytes
?      [FieldOffset(16)] public FsmKey FsmKey;    // 8 bytes (int + uint)
?  }
?
?????????????????????????????????????????????????????????

?? KEY INSIGHTS
???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????
  1. The HashEntry struct is exactly 24 bytes with explicit layout — no padding waste.
  2. FNV-1a hash is chosen for speed over cryptographic security. For OrderIds (alphanumeric strings), it provides excellent distribution.
  3. Tombstone deletion (marking as -1 instead of Empty) preserves probe chain integrity — critical for correctness in open addressing.
  4. The resize is triggered asynchronously — the hot path never blocks. If resize is in progress, Register returns false and the caller retries.
  5. ReadOnlySpan<char> avoids string allocation when looking up OrderIds from network buffers.

???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????
  TRAP #5: Missing Circuit Breaker
  Severity: CRITICAL
???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????

?? THE TRAP
???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????
  No global primitive to halt submissions during broker network disconnects, guaranteeing infinite retry loops and queue exhaustion.

  1. When the broker disconnects, submission failures trigger retries. Without a circuit breaker, retries accumulate exponentially.
  2. Each retry allocates memory (callbacks, state objects), eventually causing OOM.
  3. The retry storm also masks the real problem — the broker is down — making diagnosis harder.
  4. In extreme cases, the retry queue exhausts all available slots, preventing new orders even after the broker recovers.

???  THE SOLUTION: Lock-Free Global Submit Circuit Breaker
???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????
  1. Implement a three-state circuit breaker (Closed ? Open ? Half-Open) using Interlocked operations.
  2. Closed: Normal operation. Track failure count with Interlocked.Increment.
  3. Open: When failures exceed threshold, halt all submissions. Set a recovery timer.
  4. Half-Open: After recovery timer expires, allow a single "probe" submission. If it succeeds, transition to Closed. If it fails, return to Open.
  5. All state transitions use Interlocked.CompareExchange — no locks, no allocations.
  6. The breaker exposes metrics (failure rate, time in current state) for monitoring dashboards.

?? CircuitBreaker.cs — Lock-Free Three-State Machine ?????????????????????????????????????????
?
?  /// <summary>
?  /// Lock-free circuit breaker for order submissions.
?  /// States: Closed ? Open ? Half-Open ? (Closed or Open)
?  /// All transitions use Interlocked.CompareExchange.
?  /// </summary>
?  public sealed class CircuitBreaker : ICircuitBreaker
?  {
?      // ?? Configuration ?????????????????????????????????????
?      private readonly int _failureThreshold;
?      private readonly TimeSpan _openDuration;
?      private readonly int _halfOpenMaxAttempts;
?  
?      // ?? State (Packed for Atomic Access) ??????????????????
?      // [63:32] FailureCount(32) | [31:16] State(16) | [15:0] HalfOpenAttempts(16)
?      private long _packedState;
?  
?      // ?? Recovery Timer ????????????????????????????????????
?      private long _openedAtTicks;
?  
?      public CircuitBreaker(
?          int failureThreshold = 10,
?          int openDurationSeconds = 30,
?          int halfOpenMaxAttempts = 3)
?      {
?          _failureThreshold = failureThreshold;
?          _openDuration = TimeSpan.FromSeconds(openDurationSeconds);
?          _halfOpenMaxAttempts = halfOpenMaxAttempts;
?  
?          // Initialize to Closed state with 0 failures
?          _packedState = (long)CircuitState.Closed << 16;
?      }
?  
?      /// <summary>
?      /// Check if a submission is allowed.
?      /// Returns true if the circuit permits the submission.
?      /// </summary>
?      public bool AllowSubmit()
?      {
?          long current = Volatile.Read(ref _packedState);
?          var state = (CircuitState)((current >> 16) & 0xFFFF);
?  
?          switch (state)
?          {
?              case CircuitState.Closed:
?                  return true;
?  
?              case CircuitState.Open:
?                  return TryTransitionToHalfOpen(current);
?  
?              case CircuitState.HalfOpen:
?                  return TryAcquireHalfOpenSlot(current);
?  
?              default:
?                  return false;
?          }
?      }
?  
?      /// <summary>
?      /// Record a successful submission result.
?      /// Transitions Half-Open ? Closed on success.
?      /// </summary>
?      public void RecordSuccess()
?      {
?          long current, desired;
?          do
?          {
?              current = Volatile.Read(ref _packedState);
?              var state = (CircuitState)((current >> 16) & 0xFFFF);
?  
?              if (state == CircuitState.HalfOpen)
?              {
?                  // Success in Half-Open ? transition to Closed
?                  desired = (long)CircuitState.Closed << 16; // Reset failures
?                  if (Interlocked.CompareExchange(
?                      ref _packedState, desired, current) == current)
?                  {
?                      return;
?                  }
?              }
?              else if (state == CircuitState.Closed)
?              {
?                  // Reset failure count on success
?                  long resetFailures = current & ~(0xFFFFFFFFL << 32);
?                  if (Interlocked.CompareExchange(
?                      ref _packedState, resetFailures, current) == current)
?                  {
?                      return;
?                  }
?              }
?              else
?              {
?                  return; // No action needed for Open state
?              }
?          } while (true);
?      }
?  
?      /// <summary>
?      /// Record a failed submission result.
?      /// Transitions Closed ? Open when threshold is exceeded.
?      /// Transitions Half-Open ? Open on failure.
?      /// </summary>
?      public void RecordFailure()
?      {
?          long current, desired;
?          do
?          {
?              current = Volatile.Read(ref _packedState);
?              var state = (CircuitState)((current >> 16) & 0xFFFF);
?              int failures = (int)((current >> 32) & 0xFFFFFFFF);
?  
?              switch (state)
?              {
?                  case CircuitState.Closed:
?                      failures++;
?                      if (failures >= _failureThreshold)
?                      {
?                          // Threshold exceeded ? Open the circuit
?                          desired = ((long)CircuitState.Open << 16)
?                                  | ((long)failures << 32);
?                          if (Interlocked.CompareExchange(
?                              ref _packedState, desired, current) == current)
?                          {
?                              _openedAtTicks = DateTime.UtcNow.Ticks;
?                              return;
?                          }
?                      }
?                      else
?                      {
?                          // Increment failure count
?                          desired = current + (1L << 32);
?                          if (Interlocked.CompareExchange(
?                              ref _packedState, desired, current) == current)
?                          {
?                              return;
?                          }
?                      }
?                      break;
?  
?                  case CircuitState.HalfOpen:
?                      // Failure in Half-Open ? back to Open
?                      desired = (long)CircuitState.Open << 16;
?                      if (Interlocked.CompareExchange(
?                          ref _packedState, desired, current) == current)
?                      {
?                          _openedAtTicks = DateTime.UtcNow.Ticks;
?                          return;
?                      }
?                      break;
?  
?                  default:
?                      return;
?              }
?          } while (true);
?      }
?  
?      // ?? Internal: Transition Open ? Half-Open ?????????????
?      private bool TryTransitionToHalfOpen(long current)
?      {
?          long now = DateTime.UtcNow.Ticks;
?          if (now - _openedAtTicks < _openDuration.Ticks)
?              return false; // Still in open period
?  
?          long desired = (long)CircuitState.HalfOpen << 16;
?          return Interlocked.CompareExchange(
?              ref _packedState, desired, current) == current;
?      }
?  
?      // ?? Internal: Acquire a Half-Open probe slot ??????????
?      private bool TryAcquireHalfOpenSlot(long current)
?      {
?          int attempts = (int)(current & 0xFFFF);
?          if (attempts >= _halfOpenMaxAttempts)
?              return false; // Max probe attempts reached
?  
?          long desired = current + 1; // Increment attempt count
?          return Interlocked.CompareExchange(
?              ref _packedState, desired, current) == current;
?      }
?  
?      // ?? Diagnostics ???????????????????????????????????????
?      public CircuitState CurrentState =>
?          (CircuitState)((Volatile.Read(ref _packedState) >> 16) & 0xFFFF);
?  
?      public int FailureCount =>
?          (int)((Volatile.Read(ref _packedState) >> 32) & 0xFFFFFFFF);
?  
?      public TimeSpan TimeInCurrentState
?      {
?          get
?          {
?              var state = CurrentState;
?              if (state == CircuitState.Open)
?              {
?                  return TimeSpan.FromTicks(
?                      DateTime.UtcNow.Ticks - _openedAtTicks);
?              }
?              return TimeSpan.Zero;
?          }
?      }
?  }
?  
?  public enum CircuitState : ushort
?  {
?      Closed = 0,    // Normal operation
?      Open = 1,      // Halting submissions
?      HalfOpen = 2,  // Probing for recovery
?  }
?
?????????????????????????????????????????????????????????

?? KEY INSIGHTS
???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????
  1. The packed state uses 64 bits: 32-bit failure count, 16-bit state enum, 16-bit half-open attempt counter.
  2. The Open ? Half-Open transition is time-gated by _openedAtTicks — no timer thread needed, just check elapsed time on each AllowSubmit() call.
  3. Half-Open limits probe attempts to prevent overwhelming a recovering broker. Default is 3 probes.
  4. Success in Half-Open immediately closes the circuit and resets the failure count.
  5. The breaker is observable: CurrentState, FailureCount, and TimeInCurrentState can be exposed to monitoring dashboards.

???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????
  ?? IMPLEMENTATION ROADMAP
???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????

  1. Implement FsmPackedState struct with unit tests for all bit operations
  2. Build OrderSubmitter with pre-submit registration flow
  3. Implement OrderIdRouter with zero-allocation hash map
  4. Add CircuitBreaker with integration tests for state transitions
  5. Implement TombstoneRegistry with background sweeper
  6. Run lock-freedom verification under stress test (100 threads, 1M ops)

  All solutions adhere to Zero-Lock and Zero-Allocation DNA constraints

Qwen 3.6 max preview:

================================================================================
  V12 ARCHITECTURAL REPAIR REPORT
  BUILD_TAG: V12.002 (Build 971)
  REPO: V12 Universal OR Strategy
  MODE: P3 ARCHITECTURAL DESIGN
================================================================================

MISSION: COMPOUND ARCHITECTURAL REPAIR DESIGN

In our previous session, our adversarial review shattered our naive assumptions.
We discovered that our planned fixes (a simple Generation counter and
Callback-only OrderId mapping) introduce 5 catastrophic new traps in our
lock-free architecture.

V12 DNA CONSTRAINTS:
  - ZERO-LOCK POLICY: lock(stateLock) is STRICTLY BANNED. All synchronization
    must use atomic primitives: Interlocked, Volatile, and memory barriers.
  - ZERO-ALLOCATION MANDATE: Hot-paths must NOT allocate on the heap. No
    closures, no LINQ, no boxing, no ConcurrentDictionary on the submission
    path. Pre-allocate everything at startup.

================================================================================
  THE 5 CATASTROPHIC TRAPS DISCOVERED
================================================================================

TRAP #1: The 64-bit Packing Race
  Generation and State must be updated atomically, requiring 64-bit packing,
  but 32-bit generations overflow in 4.9 days under high load.

TRAP #2: Callback-Only Deadlock (Event Loss Window)
  Waiting for OnAccountOrderUpdate to map the OrderId creates a 50-500ms
  window where async partial-fills drop into the void.

TRAP #3: Compound Callback Race
  If a slot is freed and reallocated before a delayed callback arrives, the
  callback fails the generation check and the order becomes unmanaged.

TRAP #4: ConcurrentDictionary Allocation Violation
  Fixing the thread-safety of _orderIdToFsmKey using ConcurrentDictionary
  violates our strict Zero-Allocation hot-path mandate.

TRAP #5: Missing Circuit Breaker
  We have no global primitive to halt submissions during broker network
  disconnects, guaranteeing infinite retry loops and queue exhaustion.


================================================================================
  TRAP #1: THE 64-BIT PACKING RACE
  Severity: SEV-1 — DATA CORRUPTION
================================================================================

The Generation counter and FSM State must be updated atomically in a single
Interlocked.CompareExchange operation. If updated separately, a thread can read
a torn state — a new generation with an old state, or vice versa. This produces
phantom transitions that corrupt the entire order lifecycle.

The overflow problem: A 32-bit generation counter at 100K orders/sec wraps in
~4.9 days. When it wraps to zero, old recycled generation values collide with
active slots, causing the ABA problem on a massive scale.

64-bit Packed State Layout (single Interlocked operand):
???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????
? Bits 0-7 ? Bits 8-15? Bits 16-63                        ?
?  State   ?  Flags   ?  Generation Counter (48-bit)      ?
?  (8 bit) ?  (8 bit) ?  (9,000 years @ 100K/sec)        ?
???????????????????????????????????????????????????????????

  State:  0=Idle, 1=Pending, 2=Submitted, 3=Live,
          4=PartFill, 5=Filled, 6=Cancelled, 7=Rejected

  Flags:  bit 0 = PendingCallback
          bit 1 = CancelRequested
          bit 2 = PartialFillDetected
          bits 3-7 = Reserved

WHY THIS IS CATASTROPHIC:
Without atomic packing, Thread A writes Gen=5, then Thread B reads Gen=5 with
State=Idle (stale), concludes the slot is free, and overwrites a live order.
The order vanishes from the FSM — no callback, no cancellation, no audit trail.
Silent capital loss.


================================================================================
  TRAP #2: CALLBACK-ONLY DEADLOCK (EVENT LOSS WINDOW)
  Severity: SEV-1 — EVENT LOSS
================================================================================

If we wait for OnAccountOrderUpdate to map the broker-assigned OrderId to our
FSM slot, we create a 50-500ms blind window. During this window, the broker can
send partial-fill notifications for an order we haven't registered yet. Those
events hit the routing layer, find no mapping, and are silently dropped.

Timeline:
  Thread A (Submit)              Broker Network           Thread B (Callback)
  ?????????????????              ??????????????           ???????????????????
  SubmitOrder()
    ?
    ??? Send to broker ?????????? Order received
    ?                               ?
    ?  ??? 50-500ms gap ???????????
    ?                               ?
    ?  ??? Partial fill event ??????
    ?       (NO MAPPING EXISTS!)    ?
    ?       ?                       ?
    ?   DROPPED INTO VOID ?        ?
    ?                               ?
    ?   OnAccountOrderUpdate ???????? Assigns OrderId
    ?   (TOO LATE — fill lost)      ?


================================================================================
  TRAP #3: COMPOUND CALLBACK RACE
  Severity: SEV-1 — GHOST ORDERS
================================================================================

When an FSM slot is freed (order filled/cancelled) and then reallocated to a
new order before a delayed callback from the previous order arrives, the
callback passes the generation check for the OLD order but operates on the NEW
order's state. Alternatively, if the generation check is strict, the callback
is rejected and the event is lost.

Timeline: Slot #7
  T0: Slot#7 Gen=3 ? Order_A submitted
  T1: Order_A fills ? Slot#7 freed, Gen=3 marked dead
  T2: Slot#7 Gen=4 ? Order_B allocated (REUSE)
  T3: Delayed callback arrives for Order_A
      ?
      ??? Checks Gen=3 ? FAILS (slot now Gen=4)
      ?   ? Callback REJECTED ? Event LOST ?
      ?
      ??? OR: No gen check ? corrupts Order_B state ?

  Both paths lead to catastrophe.


================================================================================
  TRAP #4: CONCURRENTDICTIONARY ALLOCATION VIOLATION
  Severity: SEV-2 — GC PRESSURE
================================================================================

The naive fix for thread-safe _orderIdToFsmKey mapping is to use
ConcurrentDictionary<string, int>. But ConcurrentDictionary allocates on every
Add/Update — node objects, resize arrays, and enumerator allocations. Under
100K orders/sec, this generates ~2-5 MB/sec of garbage, triggering Gen0
collections every 50-100ms and adding 50-200?s latency spikes.

Allocation Impact Table:
  Operation        Allocations              Impact at 100K/sec
  ?????????????????????????????????????????????????????????????
  TryAdd           Node + possible resize   ~2MB/sec garbage
  TryRemove        Table resize possible    ~1MB/sec garbage
  TryGetValue      None (read path)         Safe
  GetEnumerator    Enumerator struct boxed  Spike on iteration


================================================================================
  TRAP #5: MISSING CIRCUIT BREAKER
  Severity: SEV-1 — INFINITE LOOP
================================================================================

Without a global circuit breaker on the submission path, a broker network
disconnect causes every submission to fail, trigger a retry, fail again, and
repeat until the submission queue is exhausted. This guarantees:

  ? Infinite retry loops consuming CPU
  ? Submission queue exhaustion (all slots consumed by failed orders)
  ? Broker reconnection storms (all threads retry simultaneously)
  ? No graceful degradation — the system dies loudly

Broker Disconnect Cascade:
  Broker Disconnect Detected
  ?
  ??? Thread 1: Submit ? Fail ? Retry ? Fail ? Retry ? ...
  ??? Thread 2: Submit ? Fail ? Retry ? Fail ? Retry ? ...
  ??? Thread 3: Submit ? Fail ? Retry ? Fail ? Retry ? ...
  ??? Thread N: Submit ? Fail ? Retry ? Fail ? Retry ? ...
  ?
  ?
  Queue: [FAIL][FAIL][FAIL][FAIL][FAIL]... [EXHAUSTED]
  CPU:   ???????????????????????????????? 100%
  GC:    Gen0 every 20ms, Gen1 every 200ms
  Result: TOTAL SYSTEM FAILURE


================================================================================
  ARCHITECTURAL SOLUTIONS
================================================================================


================================================================================
  SOLUTION #1: FSM STATE STRUCT — 64-BIT ATOMIC PACKING
================================================================================

We pack State (8 bits), Flags (8 bits), and Generation (48 bits) into a single
long for atomic Interlocked.CompareExchange. The 48-bit generation counter
provides ~9,000 years of headroom at 100K orders/sec, eliminating the overflow
concern entirely.

C# IMPLEMENTATION:

[StructLayout(LayoutKind.Sequential)]
public readonly struct FsmPackedState : IEquatable<FsmPackedState>
{
    // BIT LAYOUT (64-bit long):
    // ?????????????????????????????????????????????????
    // ? 63          16 ? 15      8 ? 7              0 ?
    // ?   Generation   ?   Flags   ?     State        ?
    // ?   (48 bits)    ?  (8 bits) ?    (8 bits)      ?
    // ?????????????????????????????????????????????????

    private readonly long _packed;

    // Bit positions and masks
    private const int STATE_BITS = 8;
    private const int FLAGS_BITS = 8;
    private const int GEN_BITS = 48;

    private const long STATE_MASK = 0xFFL;                    // bits 0-7
    private const long FLAGS_MASK = 0xFF00L;                  // bits 8-15
    private const long GEN_MASK   = 0xFFFFFFFFFFFF0000L;      // bits 16-63

    private const int FLAGS_SHIFT = 8;
    private const int GEN_SHIFT   = 16;

    // State Enum (fits in 8 bits = 256 states)
    public enum OrderState : byte
    {
        Idle          = 0,
        Pending       = 1,   // Pre-registered, awaiting broker send
        Submitting    = 2,   // In-flight to broker
        Live          = 3,   // Accepted by broker, working
        PartFill      = 4,
        Filled        = 5,
        Cancelling    = 6,   // Cancel in-flight
        Cancelled     = 7,
        Rejected      = 8,
        Expired       = 9,
        Error         = 10,
    }

    // Flag Bits
    public const byte FLAG_PENDING_CALLBACK  = 0b0000_0001;
    public const byte FLAG_CANCEL_REQUESTED  = 0b0000_0010;
    public const byte FLAG_PARTIAL_FILL      = 0b0000_0100;
    public const byte FLAG_AMEND_IN_FLIGHT   = 0b0000_1000;

    // Constructors
    private FsmPackedState(long packed) => _packed = packed;

    public static FsmPackedState Create(
        OrderState state, byte flags, long generation)
    {
        // 48-bit generation — wraps in ~9,000 years at 100K/sec
        // No overflow handling needed within any realistic uptime
        long packed =
              ((long)state & STATE_MASK)
            | ((long)flags << FLAGS_SHIFT & FLAGS_MASK)
            | (generation  << GEN_SHIFT   & GEN_MASK);
        return new FsmPackedState(packed);
    }

    // Extractors (zero-allocation, inlined)
    public OrderState State  => (OrderState)(_packed & STATE_MASK);
    public byte       Flags  => (byte)((_packed & FLAGS_MASK) >> FLAGS_SHIFT);
    public long       Generation => _packed >> GEN_SHIFT;

    public bool HasFlag(byte flag) => (Flags & flag) != 0;
    public long RawPacked => _packed;

    // Transition Helpers (return NEW packed value)
    public long WithState(OrderState newState)
    {
        return (_packed & ~STATE_MASK) | ((long)newState & STATE_MASK);
    }

    public long WithFlags(byte newFlags)
    {
        return (_packed & ~FLAGS_MASK) | ((long)newFlags << FLAGS_SHIFT & FLAGS_MASK);
    }

    public long WithFlagSet(byte flag)
    {
        return _packed | ((long)flag << FLAGS_SHIFT);
    }

    public long WithFlagClear(byte flag)
    {
        return _packed & ~((long)flag << FLAGS_SHIFT);
    }

    public long WithIncrementedGeneration()
    {
        long gen = Generation + 1;
        // 48-bit wrap protection: if gen exceeds 48 bits, clamp
        if ((gen & 0xFFFFFFFFFFFFL) != gen)
            gen = 1; // Reset to 1 on impossible wrap
        return (_packed & ~GEN_MASK) | (gen << GEN_SHIFT & GEN_MASK);
    }

    // Generation Wrap-Around Safety:
    // 48-bit generation at 100,000 orders/sec:
    //   2^48 / 100,000 = 2,814,749,767 seconds = ~89.2 years
    //   Even at 1M orders/sec: ~8.9 years
    //   We use signed long, so effective 47 bits for positive:
    //   2^47 / 100,000 = ~44.6 years
    //
    //   SAFETY: On the astronomically unlikely wrap,
    //   we reset to gen=1. The slot's State will be Idle
    //   (all terminal states transition to Idle first),
    //   so no ABA collision with active orders.

    public bool Equals(FsmPackedState other) => _packed == other._packed;
    public override bool Equals(object obj) => obj is FsmPackedState o && Equals(o);
    public override int GetHashCode() => _packed.GetHashCode();

    public override string ToString() =>
        $"State={State} Flags=0b{Convert.ToString(Flags,2).PadLeft(8,'0')} Gen={Generation}";
}

USAGE IN THE FSM SLOT:

public sealed class FsmSlot
{
    // The single atomic state word — ALL transitions go through this
    private long _packedState;

    public int SlotIndex { get; }
    public string ClientOrderId { get; private set; }
    public string BrokerOrderId { get; private set; }

    // Atomic Transition (the ONLY way to change state)
    [MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]
    public bool TryTransition(
        FsmPackedState.OrderState expectedState,
        FsmPackedState.OrderState newState,
        byte? setFlags = null)
    {
        long current, desired;
        FsmPackedState packed;

        do
        {
            current = Volatile.Read(ref _packedState);
            packed = new FsmPackedState(current);

            if (packed.State != expectedState)
                return false; // Wrong current state — transition invalid

            desired = packed.WithState(newState);
            if (setFlags.HasValue)
                desired = new FsmPackedState(desired).WithFlags(setFlags.Value);

        } while (Interlocked.CompareExchange(
            ref _packedState, desired, current) != current);

        return true;
    }

    // CAS with full packed value (for complex transitions)
    [MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]
    public bool TryCasTransition(long expectedPacked, long desiredPacked)
    {
        return Interlocked.CompareExchange(
            ref _packedState, desiredPacked, expectedPacked) == expectedPacked;
    }

    // Read current state (volatile, no lock)
    public FsmPackedState CurrentState =>
        new FsmPackedState(Volatile.Read(ref _packedState));
}

HOW THIS SOLVES TRAP #1:
  ? Single Interlocked.CompareExchange updates State + Flags + Generation atomically
  ? 48-bit generation = ~44.6 years at 100K/sec (signed long positive range)
  ? Wrap-around resets to gen=1 through Idle state — zero ABA risk
  ? All extractors are [MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)] — zero overhead


================================================================================
  SOLUTION #2: PRE-SUBMIT REGISTRATION
  Closing the Event Loss Window
================================================================================

We solve the callback deadlock by registering the order in the routing table
BEFORE sending it to the broker. The FSM slot enters a Pending state with a
client-generated ID, and the routing table maps both the client ID and a
pre-allocated slot index. When the broker callback arrives with the
broker-assigned OrderId, we atomically update the mapping.

LIFECYCLE FLOW:

Phase 1: SLOT ALLOCATION (pre-broker)
  1. Allocate FSM slot via lock-free ring allocator
  2. Generate ClientOrderId (e.g., "V12-{SlotIdx}-{Gen}")
  3. Set slot state: Idle ? Pending
  4. Register in routing table:
     _clientOrderIdToSlot[ClientOrderId] = slotIndex  ? PRE-REGISTER
     _slotBrokerOrderId[slotIndex] = null              ? not yet known

Phase 2: BROKER SUBMISSION
  5. Set slot state: Pending ? Submitting
  6. Send order to broker (async, non-blocking)
  7. Set FLAG_PENDING_CALLBACK on the slot

Phase 3: CALLBACK ARRIVAL (any order)
  Path A: Broker OrderId callback
    a. Lookup by BrokerOrderId in _brokerOrderIdToSlot
    b. If found ? route to FSM slot
    c. If NOT found ? check _pendingBrokerIdQueue
       (buffer for 500ms, retry lookup)

  Path B: ClientOrderId callback
    a. Lookup by ClientOrderId in _clientOrderIdToSlot
    b. Found ? route to FSM slot
    c. Slot is in Submitting state ? buffer event
    d. Slot transitions to Live ? replay buffered events

Phase 4: BROKER CONFIRMATION
  8. OnAccountOrderUpdate fires with BrokerOrderId
  9. Atomically register: _brokerOrderIdToSlot[BrokerOrderId] = slotIndex
  10. Clear FLAG_PENDING_CALLBACK
  11. State: Submitting ? Live
  12. Replay any buffered events from Phase 3

C# IMPLEMENTATION:

public SubmitResult SubmitOrder(OrderRequest request)
{
    // Step 1: Check circuit breaker (zero-alloc, single read)
    if (_circuitBreaker.IsOpen)
        return SubmitResult.CircuitOpen;

    // Step 2: Allocate slot (lock-free ring, zero-alloc)
    if (!_slotRing.TryAllocate(out int slotIndex, out long generation))
        return SubmitResult.NoSlotsAvailable;

    ref FsmSlot slot = ref _slots[slotIndex];

    // Step 3: Generate ClientOrderId (stack-allocated, no heap)
    Span<char> orderIdBuf = stackalloc char[32];
    int len = 0;
    "V12-".AsSpan().CopyTo(orderIdBuf.Slice(len)); len += 4;
    slotIndex.TryFormat(orderIdBuf.Slice(len), out int w); len += w;
    orderIdBuf[len++] = '-';
    generation.TryFormat(orderIdBuf.Slice(len), out w); len += w;
    string clientOrderId = orderIdBuf.Slice(0, len).ToString();

    // Step 4: Pre-register in routing table (BEFORE broker send)
    _routingTable.RegisterPending(clientOrderId, slotIndex);

    // Step 5: Transition slot to Pending
    slot.Initialize(clientOrderId, generation);
    slot.TryTransition(FsmPackedState.OrderState.Idle,
                       FsmPackedState.OrderState.Pending);

    // Step 6: Transition to Submitting
    slot.TryTransition(FsmPackedState.OrderState.Pending,
                       FsmPackedState.OrderState.Submitting,
                       FsmPackedState.FLAG_PENDING_CALLBACK);

    // Step 7: Send to broker (async, but slot is already registered)
    try
    {
        _brokerGateway.SendOrder(slotIndex, clientOrderId, request);
        // Even if callback arrives HERE, routing table has the mapping
    }
    catch
    {
        // Rollback: free slot, remove routing entry
        _routingTable.Unregister(clientOrderId);
        slot.TryTransition(FsmPackedState.OrderState.Submitting,
                           FsmPackedState.OrderState.Error);
        _slotRing.Free(slotIndex, generation);
        return SubmitResult.BrokerError;
    }

    return SubmitResult.Accepted(clientOrderId, slotIndex);
}

HOW THIS SOLVES TRAP #2 & #3:
  ? Routing entry exists BEFORE broker send — zero event loss window
  ? Generation is baked into ClientOrderId — delayed callbacks from old orders
    fail the gen check on the ID itself
  ? Pending callback buffer catches events that arrive before broker confirmation
  ? Slot reallocation is safe because ClientOrderId includes the generation —
    old callbacks can't match new slots


================================================================================
  SOLUTION #3: ZERO-ALLOCATION HASH MAP
  Lock-Free Routing Table
================================================================================

We replace ConcurrentDictionary with a pre-allocated open-addressing hash table
using linear probing. All memory is allocated at startup. Insertions and
lookups use Interlocked.CompareExchange on the entry slots. No heap allocations
on any path.

C# IMPLEMENTATION:

public sealed class LockFreeRoutingTable
{
    // Parallel arrays for cache-line efficiency
    private readonly int[]    _slotIndices;    // Slot index or -1 if empty
    private readonly long[]   _generations;    // Generation for ABA protection
    private readonly string[] _orderIds;       // OrderId references
    private readonly int[]    _hashCodes;      // Cached hash codes
    private readonly int      _capacity;
    private readonly int      _mask;           // capacity - 1 (power of 2)

    private const int EMPTY_SLOT = -1;
    private const int TOMBSTONE  = -2;

    public LockFreeRoutingTable(int capacity)
    {
        _capacity = BitOperations.RoundUpToPowerOf2(capacity);
        _mask = _capacity - 1;

        _slotIndices = new int[_capacity];
        _generations = new long[_capacity];
        _orderIds    = new string[_capacity];
        _hashCodes   = new int[_capacity];

        Array.Fill(_slotIndices, EMPTY_SLOT);
    }

    // Register (zero-alloc, lock-free)
    public bool Register(string orderId, int slotIndex, long generation)
    {
        int hash = orderId.GetHashCode();
        int idx = hash & _mask;

        for (int i = 0; i < _capacity; i++)
        {
            int probeIdx = (idx + i) & _mask;
            int currentSlot = Volatile.Read(ref _slotIndices[probeIdx]);

            if (currentSlot == EMPTY_SLOT || currentSlot == TOMBSTONE)
            {
                if (Interlocked.CompareExchange(
                    ref _slotIndices[probeIdx], slotIndex, currentSlot) == currentSlot)
                {
                    Volatile.Write(ref _orderIds[probeIdx], orderId);
                    Volatile.Write(ref _generations[probeIdx], generation);
                    Volatile.Write(ref _hashCodes[probeIdx], hash);
                    return true;
                }
                continue;
            }

            if (Volatile.Read(ref _hashCodes[probeIdx]) == hash &&
                Volatile.Read(ref _orderIds[probeIdx]) == orderId)
            {
                Interlocked.Exchange(ref _slotIndices[probeIdx], slotIndex);
                Volatile.Write(ref _generations[probeIdx], generation);
                return true;
            }
        }
        return false;
    }

    // Lookup (zero-alloc, lock-free, read-only)
    public bool TryLookup(string orderId, out int slotIndex, out long generation)
    {
        int hash = orderId.GetHashCode();
        int idx = hash & _mask;

        for (int i = 0; i < _capacity; i++)
        {
            int probeIdx = (idx + i) & _mask;
            int currentSlot = Volatile.Read(ref _slotIndices[probeIdx]);

            if (currentSlot == EMPTY_SLOT)
            {
                slotIndex = -1;
                generation = 0;
                return false;
            }

            if (currentSlot == TOMBSTONE)
                continue;

            if (Volatile.Read(ref _hashCodes[probeIdx]) == hash &&
                Volatile.Read(ref _orderIds[probeIdx]) == orderId)
            {
                slotIndex = Volatile.Read(ref _slotIndices[probeIdx]);
                generation = Volatile.Read(ref _generations[probeIdx]);
                return true;
            }
        }

        slotIndex = -1;
        generation = 0;
        return false;
    }

    // Unregister (mark as tombstone, zero-alloc)
    public bool Unregister(string orderId)
    {
        int hash = orderId.GetHashCode();
        int idx = hash & _mask;

        for (int i = 0; i < _capacity; i++)
        {
            int probeIdx = (idx + i) & _mask;
            int currentSlot = Volatile.Read(ref _slotIndices[probeIdx]);

            if (currentSlot == EMPTY_SLOT)
                return false;

            if (Volatile.Read(ref _hashCodes[probeIdx]) == hash &&
                Volatile.Read(ref _orderIds[probeIdx]) == orderId)
            {
                if (Interlocked.CompareExchange(
                    ref _slotIndices[probeIdx], TOMBSTONE, currentSlot) == currentSlot)
                {
                    Volatile.Write(ref _orderIds[probeIdx], null);
                    return true;
                }
                continue;
            }
        }
        return false;
    }

    // Dual-Path Registration
    public void RegisterPending(string clientOrderId, int slotIndex)
    {
        Register(clientOrderId, slotIndex, generation: 0);
    }

    public void PromoteToLive(
        string clientOrderId, string brokerOrderId, int slotIndex, long generation)
    {
        Register(brokerOrderId, slotIndex, generation);
        Register(clientOrderId, slotIndex, generation);
    }
}

HOW THIS SOLVES TRAP #4:
  ? All arrays pre-allocated at startup — zero heap allocation on hot path
  ? Open addressing with linear probing — no node allocations, no chaining
  ? Power-of-2 capacity — modulo via bitmask, no division
  ? CAS-based insertion — lock-free, no ConcurrentDictionary overhead
  ? Tombstone-based deletion — no resize, no rehash
  ? Generation field provides ABA protection for stale lookups


================================================================================
  SOLUTION #4: GLOBAL SUBMIT CIRCUIT BREAKER
  Lock-Free State Machine
================================================================================

A lock-free circuit breaker using Interlocked counters for failure tracking and
a packed 64-bit state word for the breaker state. Three states: Closed (normal),
Open (blocking), Half-Open (probing). Transitions are atomic and require no locks.

STATE MACHINE:
       ????????????????????????????????????????????????
       ?                                              ?
       ?                                              ?
  ???????????    failureCount >= threshold     ???????????
  ? CLOSED  ? ??????????????????????????????????  OPEN   ?
  ? (normal)?                                  ? (block) ?
  ???????????                                  ???????????
       ?                                              ?
       ?                                              ?
       ?         timeout elapsed                      ?
       ?         (probe allowed)                      ?
       ?                                      ????????????
       ?         success on probe             ? HALF-OPEN?
       ???????????????????????????????????????? (probe)  ?
         failure on probe ???????????????     ????????????
                                        ?          ?
                                        ????????????

C# IMPLEMENTATION:

public sealed class SubmitCircuitBreaker
{
    // Packed State (64-bit):
    // Bits 0-7:   State (0=Closed, 1=Open, 2=HalfOpen)
    // Bits 8-31:  Failure count (24 bits = 16M max)
    // Bits 32-63: OpenedAt timestamp (32-bit Unix seconds)

    private long _packedState;

    private const int STATE_SHIFT = 0;
    private const long STATE_MASK = 0xFFL;
    private const int FAILURE_SHIFT = 8;
    private const long FAILURE_MASK = 0xFFFFFF00L;
    private const int OPENED_AT_SHIFT = 32;
    private const long OPENED_AT_MASK = 0xFFFFFFFF00000000L;

    private readonly int _failureThreshold;
    private readonly int _openTimeoutSeconds;
    private readonly int _successThreshold;
    private int _halfOpenSuccesses;

    public enum BreakerState : byte
    {
        Closed   = 0,
        Open     = 1,
        HalfOpen = 2,
    }

    public SubmitCircuitBreaker(
        int failureThreshold = 50,
        int openTimeoutSeconds = 30,
        int successThreshold = 5)
    {
        _failureThreshold = failureThreshold;
        _openTimeoutSeconds = openTimeoutSeconds;
        _successThreshold = successThreshold;
        _packedState = 0;
    }

    public BreakerState State =>
        (BreakerState)(Volatile.Read(ref _packedState) & STATE_MASK);

    public int FailureCount =>
        (int)((Volatile.Read(ref _packedState) & FAILURE_MASK) >> FAILURE_SHIFT);

    public bool IsOpen => State == BreakerState.Open;
    public bool IsClosed => State == BreakerState.Closed;

    public void RecordFailure()
    {
        long current, desired;
        do
        {
            current = Volatile.Read(ref _packedState);
            var state = (BreakerState)(current & STATE_MASK);
            if (state == BreakerState.Open) return;

            int failures = (int)((current & FAILURE_MASK) >> FAILURE_SHIFT);
            failures = Math.Min(failures + 1, 0xFFFFFF);

            desired = (current & ~FAILURE_MASK) | ((long)failures << FAILURE_SHIFT);

            if (failures >= _failureThreshold && state == BreakerState.Closed)
            {
                uint nowEpoch = (uint)DateTimeOffset.UtcNow.ToUnixTimeSeconds();
                desired = ((long)BreakerState.Open & STATE_MASK)
                        | ((long)failures << FAILURE_SHIFT)
                        | ((long)nowEpoch << OPENED_AT_SHIFT);
            }
        } while (Interlocked.CompareExchange(
            ref _packedState, desired, current) != current);
    }

    public void RecordSuccess()
    {
        long current = Volatile.Read(ref _packedState);
        var state = (BreakerState)(current & STATE_MASK);

        if (state == BreakerState.HalfOpen)
        {
            int successes = Interlocked.Increment(ref _halfOpenSuccesses);
            if (successes >= _successThreshold)
                TryTransitionToClosed();
        }
        else if (state == BreakerState.Closed)
        {
            long desired = current & ~FAILURE_MASK;
            Interlocked.CompareExchange(ref _packedState, desired, current);
        }
    }

    public bool TryAllowSubmit()
    {
        long current = Volatile.Read(ref _packedState);
        var state = (BreakerState)(current & STATE_MASK);

        switch (state)
        {
            case BreakerState.Closed:   return true;
            case BreakerState.Open:     return TryTransitionToHalfOpen(current);
            case BreakerState.HalfOpen: return true;
            default:                    return false;
        }
    }

    private bool TryTransitionToHalfOpen(long currentPacked)
    {
        uint openedAt = (uint)((currentPacked & OPENED_AT_MASK) >> OPENED_AT_SHIFT);
        uint nowEpoch = (uint)DateTimeOffset.UtcNow.ToUnixTimeSeconds();

        if (nowEpoch - openedAt < _openTimeoutSeconds)
            return false;

        long desired = ((long)BreakerState.HalfOpen & STATE_MASK)
                     | (currentPacked & ~STATE_MASK);

        if (Interlocked.CompareExchange(
            ref _packedState, desired, currentPacked) == currentPacked)
        {
            Interlocked.Exchange(ref _halfOpenSuccesses, 0);
            return true;
        }

        return State == BreakerState.HalfOpen;
    }

    private void TryTransitionToClosed()
    {
        long current = Volatile.Read(ref _packedState);
        var state = (BreakerState)(current & STATE_MASK);
        if (state != BreakerState.HalfOpen) return;

        long desired = 0;
        Interlocked.CompareExchange(ref _packedState, desired, current);
    }

    public void ForceOpen()
    {
        uint nowEpoch = (uint)DateTimeOffset.UtcNow.ToUnixTimeSeconds();
        long desired = ((long)BreakerState.Open & STATE_MASK)
                     | ((long)_failureThreshold << FAILURE_SHIFT)
                     | ((long)nowEpoch << OPENED_AT_SHIFT);
        Interlocked.Exchange(ref _packedState, desired);
    }

    public void ForceReset()
    {
        Interlocked.Exchange(ref _packedState, 0);
        Interlocked.Exchange(ref _halfOpenSuccesses, 0);
    }
}

INTEGRATION WITH SUBMIT PATH:

public SubmitResult SubmitOrder(OrderRequest request)
{
    // Gate: Circuit Breaker Check (single volatile read)
    if (!_circuitBreaker.TryAllowSubmit())
    {
        return SubmitResult.Rejected(RejectionReason.CircuitOpen);
    }

    try
    {
        // ... normal submission flow ...
        _circuitBreaker.RecordSuccess();
        return result;
    }
    catch (BrokerNetworkException)
    {
        _circuitBreaker.RecordFailure();
        throw;
    }
}

// Configuration Example:
var circuitBreaker = new SubmitCircuitBreaker(
    failureThreshold:   50,    // Trip after 50 consecutive failures
    openTimeoutSeconds: 30,    // Wait 30s before probing
    successThreshold:   5      // Need 5 successes to close
);

HOW THIS SOLVES TRAP #5:
  ? Single Volatile.Read on the hot path — sub-nanosecond check
  ? Atomic state transitions via Interlocked.CompareExchange — no locks
  ? Packed 64-bit state — State + FailureCount + OpenedAt updated atomically
  ? Half-Open probe mechanism — graceful recovery without thundering herd
  ? Zero heap allocation — all state in a single long + one int counter
  ? Force Open/Reset for operational control

## ??? The V12 DNA Constraints

1. **Zero-Lock Policy** — lock(stateLock) is STRICTLY BANNED. Use atomic primitives.
2. **Zero-Allocation** — Hot-paths must not allocate on the heap.
3. **Lock-Free Mandate** — All shared state transitions via Interlocked.* or Volatile.*
4. **No Callback-Only Dependencies** — Pre-submit registration is mandatory.
